"https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8237703", "date": "2021-03-09 16:57:32", "main_text": "INVASIVE MOSQUITO - AUSTRALIA: (NORTHERN TERRITORY)\n***************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Mon 8 Mar 2021 11:32 PM EST [updated 9 Mar 2021]\nSource: Daily Mail [edited]\nhttps://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-9341053/Urgent-alert-deadly-mosquitos-discovered-Australian-outback-NT.html\n\n\nHealth officials have found dengue mosquitoes [_Aedes aegypti_] in the Northern Territory outback after they likely hitched a ride from tropical north Queensland. The female _Aedes aegypti_ -- also known as the yellow fever mosquito -- is the only insect that can spread dengue fever [not true. _Aedes albopictus_, the Asian tiger mosquito, can also transmit dengue viruses. - Mod.TY]\n\nDuring routine exotic mosquito surveillance in Tennant Creek, about 1000 km [620 mi] south of Darwin, 3 females and one male were trapped by medical entomology officers.\n\nNo cases of dengue fever have been diagnosed and the virus is not present in the Territory, NT Health says.\n\nIt's likely the mosquitoes were accidentally brought from Queensland by road, medical entomologist Bill Pettit said on [Tue 9 Mar 2021]. 'The dengue mosquito was eliminated from the NT in the mid-1950s and has not become permanently established since,' he said. However, it did make it back into the Territory on 3 occasions -- Tennant Creek in 2004 and 2011, and on Groote Eylandt in 2006 -- requiring 'a comprehensive 2 year program' to eliminate the insect.\n\nHealth officers will travel to Tennant Creek this month to search for more dengue mosquitoes and larvae.\n\nThe insect is often found around homes and typically lay their eggs in water-filled containers such as buckets, animal dishes and flower pots. The eggs can survive in the dry for up 12 months and follow-up visits are likely to be required after the next rains to ensure the mosquito is eliminated. Tennant Creek residents have been urged to tip out any water from containers around their homes until their properties have been inspected.\n\nDengue fever is usually found in tropical and subtropical countries in Africa, Asia, and South America. An outbreak also occurs in North Queensland each year. Symptoms are high fever, a rash, and muscle and joint pain. In severe cases, there is serious bleeding and shock, which can be life-threatening.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This discovery of _Aedes aegypti_ in the Northern Territory (NT) after a long absence illustrates the ease with which this mosquito can be moved through human activity. NT health authorities are prudent to respond aggressively and eliminate this mosquito while its numbers are small and its location is limited. This mosquito is established in northern Queensland and transmits dengue viruses there -- something to be avoided in dengue-free NT. - Mod.TY\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nNorthern Territory, Australia: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/292]\nSee Also\n2015\n---\nInvasive mosquito - Australia, Belgium 20150820.3590389\n.................................................sb/sh/ty/ao/sh", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8236250", "headline": "COVID-19 update (91): USA post vacc, vacc passport, WHO", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8236250", "date": "2021-03-09 07:02:58", "main_text": "CORONAVIRUS DISEASE 2019 UPDATE (91): USA POST VACCINATION, EUROPE VACCINATION PASSPORTS, WHO\n*********************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nIn this update:\n[1] USA: CDC post vaccination recommendations\n[2] Europe: vaccination passport\n[3] COVID news snippets\n[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 8 Mar 2021)\n[5] Global update: Worldometer accessed 8 Mar 2021 22:30 EST (GMT-5)\n\n******\n[1] USA: CDC post vaccination recommendations\n[A] Media report\nDate: Mon 8 Mar 2021 11:08 AM ET\nSource: NPR (National Public Radio) [edited]\nhttps://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2021/03/08/974783644/cdc-says-its-safe-for-vaccinated-people-to-do-these-activities\n\n\nThe Centers for Disease Control and Prevention has issued new guidance for vaccinated people, giving the green light to resume some pre-pandemic activities and relax precautions that have been in place.\n\nSpecifically, the new guidance says, people who are fully vaccinated can visit indoors with other fully vaccinated people without wearing masks or social distancing. People are considered fully vaccinated 2 weeks after they have gotten the 2nd shot of the Pfizer or Moderna vaccines (or 2 weeks after receiving the single-dose Johnson & Johnson vaccine).\n\nVaccinated people can also visit, unmasked, with people from another household who are not yet vaccinated, as long as those people are at low risk of serious illness from the virus. However, the agency said, vaccinated people should continue to wear masks when they're in public, avoid crowds, and take other precautions when gathering with unvaccinated people who are at high risk of serious illness from COVID-19.\n\nThe new guidance also allows fully vaccinated individuals to forgo testing and quarantining following a known COVID-19 exposure, as long as they are not experiencing symptoms.\n\nCDC said this new guidance is a \"1st step\" to returning to everyday activities. There's accumulating evidence to show that people who are fully vaccinated are less likely to become infected and also \"potentially\" less likely to spread the virus to others, agency officials wrote in a press release. \"We know that people want to get vaccinated so they can get back to doing the things they enjoy with the people they love,\" CDC director Dr Rochelle Walensky said in a statement about the new guidelines.\n\nThe new guidance is specific to freedoms that vaccinated people can resume in their own homes, but the agency warns that everyone -- even those who are vaccinated -- should continue to follow recommended guidelines in public settings, including wearing masks.\n\nCDC is not updating its travel guidance at this time, Walensky said at a White House COVID-19 Response Team briefing on Monday [8 Mar 2021]. She stressed that everyone should continue to avoid nonessential trips, regardless of vaccination status. The CDC director cited previous spikes in case counts after surges in travel and the emergence of variants from international locations. Existing travel guidance still applies in the case of fully vaccinated grandparents who are hoping to visit their low-risk family members, Walensky said in response to a reporter's question. \"We would like to give the opportunity to vaccinated grandparents to visit their grandchildren and children who are healthy and who are local, but our travel guidance currently has been unchanged,\" she said.\n\nThe 3 available vaccines have been proven to protect against severe illness, hospitalization, and death from COVID-19, Walensky added. But she said there is still a small risk that vaccinated people could become infected with a mild or asymptomatic disease and potentially even pass it on to others who are not vaccinated. She said this remains an ongoing area of research. Walensky said this is the 1st round of guidance, but more will follow as the science evolves and more people are fully vaccinated. \"We believe these recommendations are an important 1st step in our efforts to resume everyday activities in our communities,\" she said. \"However, we remain in the midst of a serious pandemic, and still over 90% of our population is not fully vaccinated, though we are working hard to get there.\"\n\nThe Biden administration is working to scale up vaccine manufacturing and distribution and announced last week [week of 1 Mar 2021] that the country will have enough supply for every adult by the end of May [2021]. The country's 7-day average of daily vaccinations is nearly 2.2 million, and a record-breaking 2.9 million doses were administered on Saturday [6 Mar 2021], according to Andy Slavitt, White House senior adviser on the White House COVID-19 Response Team. Walensky said that as of Monday [8 Mar 2021], about 59 million people in the US have received at least one dose of the COVID-19 vaccine. And about 31 million people -- or 9.2% of the U.S. population -- are fully vaccinated.\n\nHere's CDC's specific guidance for what fully vaccinated people can do:\n-\"visit with other fully vaccinated people indoors without wearing masks or physical distancing;\n- \"visit with unvaccinated people from a single household who are at low risk for severe COVID-19 disease indoors without wearing masks or physical distancing;\n- \"refrain from quarantine and testing following a known exposure to COVID-19 if asymptomatic.\"\n\nCDC said fully vaccinated people should continue to take these COVID-19 precautions:\n- \"take precautions in public like wearing a well-fitted mask and physical distancing;\n- \"wear masks, practice physical distancing, and adhere to other prevention measures when visiting with unvaccinated people who are at increased risk for severe COVID-19 disease or who have an unvaccinated household member who is at increased risk for severe COVID-19 disease;\n- \"wear masks, maintain physical distance, and practice other prevention measures when visiting with unvaccinated people from multiple households;\n- \"avoid medium- and large-sized in-person gatherings;\n- \"get tested if experiencing COVID-19 symptoms;\n- \"follow guidance issued by individual employers;\n- \"follow CDC and health department travel requirements and recommendations.\"\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nSukie Crandall\n<sukie@mac.com>\n\n----\n[B] CDC\nDate: Mon 8 Mar 2021\nSource: CDC [edited]\nhttps://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/vaccines/fully-vaccinated.html\n\n\nWhen you've been fully vaccinated -- How to protect yourself and others\n----------------------------------------------------------------\nCOVID-19 vaccines are effective at protecting you from getting sick. Based on what we know about COVID-19 vaccines, people who have been fully vaccinated can start to do some things that they had stopped doing because of the pandemic.\n\nWe're still learning how vaccines will affect the spread of COVID-19. After you've been fully vaccinated against COVID-19, you should keep taking precautions in public places like wearing a mask, staying 6 feet [2 m] apart from others, and avoiding crowds and poorly ventilated spaces until we know more.\n\nWhat's changed\n--------------\nIf you've been fully vaccinated:\n- You can gather indoors with fully vaccinated people without wearing a mask.\n- You can gather indoors with unvaccinated people from one other household (for example, visiting with relatives who all live together) without masks unless any of those people or anyone they live with has an increased risk for severe illness from COVID-19.\n- If you've been around someone who has COVID-19, you do not need to stay away from others or get tested unless you have symptoms.\n- However, if you live in a group setting (like a correctional or detention facility or group home) and are around someone who has COVID-19, you should still stay away from others for 14 days and get tested, even if you don't have symptoms.\n\nWhat hasn't changed\n-------------------\nFor now, if you've been fully vaccinated:\n- You should still take steps to protect yourself and others in many situations, like wearing a mask, staying at least 6 feet a[2 m] part from others, and avoiding crowds and poorly ventilated spaces. Take these precautions whenever you are:\n-- in public;\n-- gathering with unvaccinated people from more than one other household;\n-- visiting with an unvaccinated person who is at increased risk of severe illness or death from COVID-19 or who lives with a person at increased risk.\n- You should still avoid medium or large-sized gatherings.\n- You should still delay domestic and international travel. If you do travel, you'll still need to follow CDC requirements and recommendations.\n- You should still watch out for symptoms of COVID-19, especially if you've been around someone who is sick. If you have symptoms of COVID-19, you should get tested and stay home and away from others.\n- You will still need to follow guidance at your workplace.\n\nWhat we know and what we're still learning\n------------------------------------------\n- We know that COVID-19 vaccines are effective at preventing COVID-19 disease, especially severe illness and death.\n- We're still learning how effective the vaccines are against variants of the virus that causes COVID-19. Early data show the vaccines may work against some variants but could be less effective against others.\n- We know that other prevention steps help stop the spread of COVID-19 and that these steps are still important, even as vaccines are being distributed.\n- We're still learning how well COVID-19 vaccines keep people from spreading the disease.\n- Early data show that the vaccines may help keep people from spreading COVID-19, but we are learning more as more people get vaccinated.\n- We're still learning how long COVID-19 vaccines can protect people.\n- As we know more, CDC will continue to update our recommendations for both vaccinated and unvaccinated people.\n\nUntil we know more about those questions, everyone -- even people who've had their vaccines -- should continue taking basic prevention steps when recommended.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The cautions I am concerned about deal with the final section above: \"What we know and what we're still learning\". The media have picked up the \"do's and don'ts\", but haven't mentioned the as yet still unknowns that may influence these current recommendations. Especially those concerning the variants and impact on vaccine efficacy. Are the T-cells primed by the vaccines currently available protective against the variants in circulation or are even vaccinated individuals at risk? If the latter... - Mod.MPP]\n\n******\n[2] Europe: vaccination passport\nDate: Sun 7 Mar 2021 11:00 AM GMT+1\nSource: The Washington Post [edited]\nhttps://www.washingtonpost.com/world/europe/europe-vaccine-passport-travel/2021/03/05/60db1d8a-7aaa-11eb-8c5e-32e47b42b51b_story.html\n\n\nEurope debates vaccine passports as a way to save summer tourism\n----------------------------------------------------------------\nAhead of Europe's summer holiday season, some top destinations such as Greece and Spain are pushing the European Union to introduce digital \"vaccine passports\" to ease entry for visitors -- and their tourism cash. But what some countries see as a path toward reopening has been viewed by others, led by France and Germany, as a path toward a 2-tier system that could leave the unvaccinated as outsiders in places such as gyms, restaurants, and cinemas. \"Immunity passports could reinforce inequalities both within and between countries,\" said Emilian Kavalski, a professor at the University of Nottingham's campus in Ningbo, China.\n\nSome countries have already taken steps in that direction. In Britain, now outside the EU, foreign secretary Dominic Raab said vaccine certificates are \"under consideration\" even as other British officials dismissed the idea. Israel recently launched digital vaccination certificates to allow access to gyms or restaurants.\n\nIsrael also agreed to trial a travel bubble with EU members Greece and Cyprus to open the door for vaccinated travelers. Meanwhile, Cyprus has also said it will begin in May [2021] to welcome vaccinated visitors from Britain.\n\nThe European Commission is expected to submit a proposal on how to bridge the divides with the bloc this month [March 2021], which could lay out a joint plan for digital vaccination certificates that would work across the EU and potentially beyond.\n\nCompromise proposals could include exceptions for individuals who have recovered from COVID-19 or those who can provide a recent negative test result. It is unclear what a digital vaccine certificate would look like. Personalized QR codes -- used in Israel and difficult to forge -- would be one possible option.\n\nBut finding common ground across the EU will not be easy. Vaccination rates vary widely. So does the political will to put the vaccinated in the fast lane for travel -- with countries most dependent on tourism cash leading the way. \"Those who are vaccinated should have full freedom,\" said Austria's chancellor Sebastian Kurz, who has joined Greece and Spain in support of vaccination documents. \"Some countries are very much preoccupied with now,\" Greece's tourism minister, Harry Theocharis, told the Financial Times last month [February 2021], in an apparent reference to German and French hesitancy.\n\nTourism accounts for about 20 per cent of Greece's GDP, which declined by 10 per cent last year [2020]. \"People will gradually realize that there is not much of an alternative,\" Andreas Papatheodorou, a Greek tourism researcher, said. If no EU-wide solution can be found, Greece and other countries may opt for bilateral deals, he said.\n\nGerman chancellor Angela Merkel has signalled openness to study possible vaccination certificates later this year [2021]. But she has insisted treating vaccinated travelers preferentially now \"isn't on the agenda, given the low vaccination coverage at this point\". French officials have made the same argument. They also appear worried about how a proposed pass would be received by the large number of vaccine skeptics in the country. Only around half the population was willing to get vaccinated when the rollout began 2 months ago. French vaccine approval has recently inched upward. Some officials still fear a \"vaccination passport\" would risk undoing that progress.\n\nSome groups -- including members of ethnic minorities or pregnant women -- would be disproportionately impacted, because COVID vaccination rates among them are lower than in the general population, according to recent studies. Young people who are last in line to receive vaccines or older people with no smartphones would also be disadvantaged.\n\nThere is also still no scientific consensus on the extent to which vaccines reduce transmission of the virus, raising the possibility that vaccinated travelers might spread the virus even if they do not get sick themselves, said Melinda Mills, director of the Leverhulme Centre for Demographic Science at Oxford University.\n\nPresident Biden said last week that there will be enough vaccines for all US adults by May [2021]. The European Commission hopes to vaccinate 70 per cent of the EU's adult population by the end of the summer [2021], which would still leave more than 100 million Europeans without immunization in late September [2021].\n\n\"If you introduce this right away, you'd be excluding a huge group just on age-based discrimination,\" Mills said of possible \"vaccine passports,\" adding that court challenges would probably follow.\n\nOther questions are piling up, too. Would EU citizens qualify for a certificate if they receive vaccines not approved by the EU drug regulator, such as Russia's Sputnik V and Chinese vaccines? What happens if variants spread that reduce some vaccines' efficacy?\n\nThen there are privacy concerns. For decades, paper certificates have been used for travel to show vaccinations against yellow fever and other diseases. But a digital certification, potentially with QR-codes, raises worries about whether the data could be used to track travelers' movements.\n\nSome global companies have already vowed to make use of their right to ban customers. Alan Joyce, the head of Australia's carrier Qantas, said last year [2020] that proof of vaccination would soon become a prerequisite for flying. \"I think that's going to be a common thing, talking to my colleagues in other airlines around the globe,\" he said. Similar requirements could be introduced for people entering sports stadiums or workplaces.\n\nThe idea of requiring travelers to carry health certificates is a relatively modern concept, said Kavalski, who has researched the historical evolution of passports. Passports were widely introduced during World War I in what some saw as a temporary measure. But the 1918 flu pandemic helped shape international travel with \"the practice of allowing only 'healthy' bodies to cross borders,\" Kavalski said. \"I would say the [current] pandemic will have a lasting impact on the practices and experience of border crossing,\" Kavalski said.\n\n[byline: Rick Noack]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Clearly, the use of vaccination passports is highly controversial as we see discussions play out in Europe at present. The concerns about privacy violations can and could be accepted as for the better public good. With our digital footprints currently, it is a false sense of security that privacy is preserved as evidenced by all of the tracking apps, etc, that have been put into play during the pandemic. The discrimination argument is valid before all adults have access to vaccine. As for those that refuse vaccine, they have exercised their right to refuse, but is there an inherent right for them to put others at risk? There are anecdotal reports of individuals who, knowing themselves to be ill with SARS-CoV-2 infection, have boarded planes to travel. Unfortunately, where there's a will there's a way. While the feeling is that the bar code passports are harder to forge, what about healthcare personnel who are not supporting vaccinations providing such passport authorizations? I am probably making many enemies by my comments here, but I hope I am communicating there are many issues to be resolved before such passports could and should be adopted. I suggest reading a 22 Jan 2021 article raising concerns re the use of health passport (https://www.washingtonpost.com/travel/2021/01/22/passport-vaccine-covid-flights-international/?itid=lk_interstitial_manual_53). It points out the concerns re dropping quarantine and testing requirements for travellers who are fully vaccinated -- a legitimate concern as we still don't know the impact of vaccination on transmission of the virus, especially the variants. Not a black and white debate here. - Mod.MPP]\n\n******\n[3] COVID-19 news snippets\nDate: Tue 9 Mar 2021\nSource: The Washington Post [edited]\nhttps://www.washingtonpost.com/nation/2021/03/08/coronavirus-covid-live-updates-us/\n\n\nHealth experts worry about variant-driven surge as states lift restrictions\n--------------------------------------------------------------\nAs authorities relax restrictions meant to curb the coronavirus and the race to vaccinate the public remain under way, experts say the US sits at a potential inflection point, with highly contagious variants threatening an additional surge. Michael T Osterholm, director of the Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy [CIDRAP] at the University of Minnesota and an adviser to President Biden's coronavirus task force, said during a Sunday [7 Mar 2021] interview with NBC's \"Meet the Press\" that the nation is \"in the eye of the hurricane\". Other epidemiologists cited concern over the looming spring break season, saying it could accelerate the spread of the new variants.\n\nHere are some significant developments:\n- The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention released guidance on what fully vaccinated Americans can do, saying they can visit nearby grandchildren and dine with one another indoors.\n- Syrian leader Bashar al-Assad and his wife, Asma, have tested positive for the coronavirus, his office announced on Monday [8 Mar 2021]. Both are in a stable condition, the statement said.\n- Scientists knew that the coronavirus would mutate, they just had no idea it would happen so fast, and now they fear the loose cannon variants could wreck hard-won progress.\n- A top medical official with the European Union cautioned against some member states' approval of Russia's Sputnik V vaccine ahead of the bloc's own official review process.\n- The support for President Biden's USD 1.9 trillion coronavirus relief package in much of the country suggests a shift in attitude over the role of the government in helping the economy.\n- A look inside the shifting messaging and struggle to implement one of Biden's central promises: to get children back into classrooms as soon as possible.\n- More than a half-million Americans have died from the coronavirus while nearly 29 million cases have been reported.\n\n- 9:15 a.m.\nStories of time lost: A girl, almost 9, who never felt like she got to be 8. A 102 year old who lives in isolation. And everyone in between.\n\nThe coronavirus pandemic brought out stories of profound grief and heroic resolve.\nThese are not those stories.\n\nInstead, at this one-year mark, Style [Washington Post] reporters set out to note some of the other, countless emotions and personal losses: The almost-9 year old who never felt like she got to be 8. The 102 year old who lives in mandated isolation. The massage therapist and her customers who simply crave touch. The couple who postponed their big wedding -- and may have to postpone it again. The single person losing her last sense of social contact. The DJ who spins for an empty room. The college freshman who has never set foot on campus. Shutdowns, lockdowns, quarantines -- whatever you called this long and lost time, these stories acknowledge the persistent disconnect, all that absence, and what it feels like to live in a suspended state of mind.\n\n- 8:45 a.m.\nChina awash in 'cherry freedom' despite virus fears\nAmong Chinese youths, the term \"cherry freedom\" has meant the aspirational level of financial security where you can buy premium fruits whenever the whim strikes. So it came as a shock when cherry freedom suddenly arrived for everyone. In January [2021], Chinese media reported that packaging from a shipment of Chilean cherries had tested positive for the coronavirus. In the confusion that followed, Chinese retailers dumped cherry orders and consumers shunned the fruit. Chinese health experts went on TV to say cherries were safe to eat if you washed them (the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention says the risk from eating or handling food is \"very low\"), while Chile's embassy said it hadn't been confirmed that the tainted batch was from Chile. But it was too late: Prices collapsed as 288 000 tons of imported Chilean cherries approached their expiration date.\n[byline: Lyric Li, Eva Dou]\n\n- 8:00 a.m.\nAnalysis: What the media should not do when battling vaccine misinformation\nThere are all sorts of ways to counter reluctance to get the coronavirus vaccine. There's leading by example. There's guilt. And there's pure charm. Dolly Parton went the latter route last week [2 Mar 2021] as she got her 1st shot, wearing a sparkly blue cold-shoulder dress for her Instagram PSA and crooning \"Vaccine\" to the tune of her signature \"Jolene\". Despite all this high-level persuasion, a big chunk of Americans -- about 3 in 10 -- remain hesitant, according to a new Pew Research survey. The news media has a role to play -- not in outright advocacy, but in relentlessly providing accurate, nuanced information and answering questions straightforwardly. \"There is a lot to be said for honestly reporting as much context as possible and knowing the terrain into which your sound bites and headlines will play,\" said Emily Bell, director of the Tow Center for Digital Journalism at Columbia University.\n[byline: Margaret Sullivan]\n\n- 7:15 a.m.\nPeople threaten to call ICE [US Immigration and Customs Enforcement] after a Mexican restaurant in Texas keeps its mask rules\nWhen the coronavirus pandemic hit and restaurant owners faced difficult decisions, the Richards family that owns Picos, a Mexican restaurant in Houston, quickly adapted to continue sharing their Latin cuisine -- from selling to-go margarita kits to stationing a mariachi band at the curbside pickup. This week, after Texas governor Greg Abbott (R) said on Tuesday [2 Mar 2021] that he would rescind the statewide mask mandate, while the vast majority of residents remain unvaccinated, the tough choice to enforce public health guidance fell to business owners, and Picos announced it would continue requiring masks. But, after such a challenging year, the reaction to their decision was disheartening, co-owner Monica Richards said: Several people sent hateful messages through social media and called the restaurant, threatening to report staffers to Immigration and Customs Enforcement.\n[byline: Meryl Kornfield]\n\n- 6:31 a.m.\nThe whiplash of Pope Francis's Iraq trip: A year of tight COVID-19 rules in Italy, then 72 hours of crowds\nAboard the papal plane -- By almost every measurement, Pope Francis's trip to Iraq was stunning. He went to a country no pope had visited before, at a time when few other global figures were traveling. He led prayer in the very place where, just 7 years earlier, the Islamic State's leader had proclaimed a caliphate that would \"conquer Rome\". The crowds were adoring, ululating, sometimes crying. The theater was unbeatable. And yet, amid all this, I kept thinking about the coronavirus. Almost everywhere Francis went, there were crowds. Big crowds of unvaccinated people, shoulder-to-shoulder. Francis's outdoor Mass in Irbil, capital of the semiautonomous Iraqi region of Kurdistan, had nearly the attendance of the Super Bowl, but in a dramatically smaller stadium; few were wearing masks. Most startling was an indoor Mass on Saturday night [5 Mar 2021] in Baghdad, in a packed church with people singing and almost no ventilation. I was a pool reporter for that service; it felt like standing in a coronavirus nuclear reactor[see photograph at https://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-apps/imrs.php?src=https://arc-anglerfish-washpost-prod-washpost.s3.amazonaws.com/public/DC446WT73UI6XPRCGLJTDWDVGA.jpg&w=916\n[byline: Chico Harlan]\n\n- 5:47 a.m.\nHow a year lived online has changed our children\nLike many parents just trying to get to the other side of a pandemic in one piece, [I L-L] doesn't have the bandwidth to micromanage screen time for her 2 older kids. By giving up some, but not all, control, she and other parents have been able to see firsthand the good and bad of letting kids lead the way with their own technology usage. \"Screen time\" -- as a concept to track meticulously, to fret and panic about, to measure parents' worth in -- is no longer considered a valid framework in a pandemic world, where the way we live our lives has been completely redefined. Since schools in the United States began closing down roughly a year ago, the country's children have been adapting, learning, and getting creative with how they use technology. The realities of their day-to-day lives have varied wildly, as have their relationships with screens.\n[byline: Heather Kelly]\n\n- 4:45 a.m.\nJapan battles new variants as vaccine program is in disarray\nJapan's coronavirus vaccination program is in disarray -- mostly from self-inflicted wounds. Vaccinations are at a crawl, upending hopeful predictions that life could start to return to normal by the summer. Even before a 3rd wave of infections is under control, many health experts are predicting another possible surge ahead of the summer's Olympics. Japan's government boasts of its success in containing the worst of the pandemic. But medical experts tell a different story -- a failure to meet the moment, and of a slow-moving government and bureaucracy struggling to adapt to a fast-moving pandemic. It adds up to a jolting contrast as many other wealthy nations have their feet on the gas to accelerate and expand vaccinations. Japan's very slow rollout also is likely to undermine support for beleaguered prime minister Yoshihide Suga and delay Japan's economic recovery.\n\n- 4:02 a.m.\nIsrael begins vaccinating 100 000 Palestinian day laborers\nIsrael on Monday [8 Mar 2021] kicked off its 2-week campaign to vaccinate more than 100 000 Palestinians carrying Israeli work permits even as coronavirus vaccinations remained a distant dream for most residents of the West Bank. At the crossing of Sha'ar Efraim, the Israeli military set up one of 8 vaccination centers -- with the capacity to vaccinate 1000 people a day -- along the 440-mile [708 km] barrier dividing Israel from the Palestinian territories. \"It is within both Israeli and Palestinian interests that we vaccinate the workers, since, as we know, coronavirus knows no geographical boundaries,\" said Lior Wisbaum, foreign relations officer for the coordinator of government activities in the Territories, or COGAT, the Israeli military agency that coordinates with the Palestinian Authority.\n[byline: Shira Rubin]\n\n- 2:57 a.m.\nWhite House: 'Hopeful day' as vaccinations jump, Senate passes American Rescue Plan, CDC issues guidance\nThe Biden administration on Monday [8 Mar 2021] touted the increased pace of vaccinations and the Senate's passage of the American Rescue Plan as promising signs in the \"war\" on the coronavirus. \"President Biden came into office with 2 clear immediate goals -- mount a vaccination program to turn the tide on the pandemic and pass a rescue plan to bring the nation through these tough times successfully,\" Andy Slavitt, senior White House adviser for the coronavirus response, told reporters at a press briefing. \"This weekend, we took critical steps on both fronts.\" Slavitt noted that the nation's vaccination pace has sped up, with nearly 2.2 million shots a day administered in the past week, up from about 900 000 when Biden took office [20 Jan 2021]. Slavitt also said that Congress's USD1.9 trillion legislative package, directed by Biden, would address poverty while ramping up other resources to fight the pandemic. Marcella Nunez-Smith, who's leading the Biden administration's work on health equity and the coronavirus, pointed to progress rolling out community vaccination centers that are focused on hard-hit, high-risk communities. \"By the end of this week, we'll have 18 of those sites running across 7 states, with the ability to administer 61 000 total shots per week,\" Nunez-Smith said. Nunez-Smith also said that the administration is still working on its planned messaging campaign to address vaccine hesitancy. Nearly one-third of GOP voters say they \"definitely won't\" get the vaccine, and polls have found widespread skepticism in communities of color, as well. Meanwhile, Anthony S Fauci, the nation's leading infectious-disease expert, offered a brief update on researchers' efforts to develop antivirals that hinder the progression of COVID-19 symptoms and help infected people avoid needing to be hospitalized. \"That is the direction that we will be going over the next weeks to months to years,\" Fauci said, comparing the fight to the effort to combat HIV. At the briefing, Centers for Disease Control and Prevention Director Rochelle Walensky also unveiled long-awaited guidance on how vaccinated Americans can socialize and pursue daily activities. \"I hope people view this as a hopeful day in the next steps of the pandemic,\" Slavitt said.\n[byline: Dan Diamond]\n\n- 2:52 a.m.\nSWAT [special weapons and tactics, a law enforcement unit]] team called into maskless Boulder college party where students set off fireworks and flipped a car\nBy the time police arrived, the party had been raging for hours. Beginning late Saturday afternoon [6 Mar 2021], music bumped as 500 -- 800 maskless revelers swarmed a street in a neighborhood near the University of Colorado at Boulder. The cheering crowd later blasted fireworks into the sky and flipped a car. Law enforcement officers showed up with a SWAT vehicle at about 8:30 pm local time. Using a loudspeaker, they warned, \"If you fail to leave, you will be subject to arrest and the use of tear gas.\" Many students cleared out. Others stayed, shouting expletives at police. About 100 ran toward authorities, police said, and several threw bottles and rocks. The chaos, which unfolded a day after Colorado Gov. Jared Polis (D) paid tribute to the state's nearly 6000 COVID-19 victims, ended with police reporting minor injuries to several officers, along with damage to community and public-safety vehicles.\n[byline: Brittany Shammas]\n\n- 1:19 a.m.\nInside Biden's struggle to meet his school reopening promises\nThe promise was clear and hopeful: With strong public health measures, then-president-elect Joe Biden declared in early December [2020], \"the majority of our schools can be open by the end of my 1st 100 days.\" The reality has been far more complicated. First came the clarification on Biden's 1st full day as president, when the administration released a 200-page coronavirus response plan that explained the schools reopening plan included only K-8 schools -- not high schools -- in those 1st 100 days. Then came a walk-back from White House press secretary Jen Psaki, who said the administration's goal was only to have the majority of schools back in classrooms \"at least one day a week.\" And finally came Biden's walk-back of the walk-back in a CNN town hall, where he described the one-day-a-week standard as a \"mistake in the communication.\"\n[byline: Ashley Parker, Laura Meckler, Fenit Nirappil, Annie Linskey]\n\n- 12:18 a.m.\nMeet the GOP [Republican Party] voters who could decide whether the US reaches herd immunity\n[M], an 80 year old retiree who lives outside Tulsa, has spent the past year living in fear of the coronavirus. She's constantly worn masks, toted hand sanitizer, and used drive-throughs to run her errands. Her age and preexisting health conditions -- including heart failure, diabetes, and blood clots -- put her at elevated risk if she gets sick. But unlike many at-risk Americans seeking safety and an end to the pandemic, [M] refuses to get a coronavirus vaccine. \"There's too many unanswered questions,\" said [M]. [She] also said she's fearful of possible side effects such as the headaches that some people have gotten from the 2nd shot. \"I'd just as soon as not go through that,\" she said.\n[byline: Dan Diamond]\n\n[RELATED]\n\nDate: Sun 7 Mar 2021\nSource: Meet the Press [abridged, edited]\nhttps://www.nbcnews.com/meet-the-press/meet-press-march-7-2021-n1259907\n\n\nJeffrey Zients, Michael Osterholm, senator Joe Manchin (D-WV), senator John Barrasso (R-WY), Yamiche Alcindor, Jeh Johnson, Danielle Pletka, and Jonathan Allen\n\nOsterholm: UK variant 'is about to come upon us'\n\nIn an interview with Meet the Press, Michael Osterholm, Director, Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy at the University of Minnesota, talks to Chuck Todd about the UK variant and its spread in the US.\n\n[byline: Rick Noack, Paul Schemm, Brittany Shammas, Reis Thebault]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail rapporteur Kunihiko Iizuka\n\n[This set of news snippets from the Washington Post covers an array of how responses to COVID-19 vary among different states and different individuals. That being said, positive environmental samples mean that the virus is actively circulating. But, 2020 was a major year for cVDPV outbreaks with a total to date of 1067 confirmed AFP cases associated with circulating vaccine derived polioviruses and in 2021, as of 3 Mar, 13 cases have already been reported. Countries involved included Eurasia (Tajikistan), Middle East (Egypt, Yemen), Asia (Pakistan, Afghanistan, Malaysia), Africa (Angola, Benin, Burkina Faso, Cameroon, Central African Republic, Chad, Congo, Cote d'Ivoire, DR Congo, Ethiopia, Ghana, Guinea, Kenya, Liberia, Mali, Niger, Nigeria, Sierra Leone, Somalia. South Sudan, Sudan, Togo), and the Pacific (Philippines).\n\nSee Dr T Jacob John's comment re: vaccine derived poliovirus cases and estimated size of the outbreaks below.\n\nFor a global map showing distribution of the poliovirus outbreaks during the past 12 months (both WPV1 and cVDPV associated, see http://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/. - Mod.MPP]\n\n******\n[3] Comment on cVDPV\nDate: Wed 24 Feb 2021\nFrom: T Jacob John <tjacobjohn@yahoo.co.in> [edited]\n\n\n[My sincere apologies for the delay in posting this update and comment from Dr T Jacob John. - Mod.MPP]\n\nThe case-to-infection ratio of wild poliovirus type 2 [WPV2] is in the range of 1 to 1000-2000. So one case of WPV2 polio means 1000-2000 silent infections. cVDPV has a lower risk of paralysis, the case-to-infection ratio may be between 1 to 5000-10 000. That is the reason why we cannot rely on AFP surveillance for detecting the prevalence of cVDPV-2 but need sewage surveillance.\n\nIn 2020, if there were 1048 confirmed cases of polio due to cVDPV-2, that means the size of the silent epidemic was at least 1048 x 5000 = 5 240 000 [updating this calculation to 1067 cases, 5 335 000 infections - Mod.MPP]\n\nWaiting for novel OPV [oral poliovirus vaccines] is not enough. There is no guarantee the eradication program can eradicate cVDPV-2 in one or 2 years. If we had 5 million cVDPV infections in 2020, the probability that it will further de-attenuate and become genotypically and phenotypically closer to wild virus than vaccine virus is high. Immediate and widespread IPV [inactivated polio vaccine] by campaign is the necessary intervention now.\n\nIf that is not operationally feasible, EPI [Expanded Program on Immunization] must revise its immunisation policy to recommend \"at least 2 doses\" of IPV, stand-alone or combination vaccine. I say this because \"at least 1 dose of IPV\" is part of the eradication program.\n\nIf stand-alone, then 14 weeks and 9 months of age should be ideal, to match with 2 contacts for other vaccines, or if combination vaccine, 3 doses as per the current EPI schedule. This is ethically necessary. No excuses like high cost or low coverage, etc. should be used to delay this decision. No child ever had polio after 2 well-timed IPV doses or 3 EPI schedule IPV doses. Preventing polio is the primary duty of the eradication program; this will not in any way interfere with the interventions deemed necessary by the eradication program.\n\n--\nT Jacob John\n439, Civil Supplies Godown Lane\nKamalakshipuram\nVellore, TN 632002\nIndia\n<tjacobjohn@yahoo.co.in>\n\n[ProMED would like to thank Dr T Jacob John for his very insightful comment. Clearly, the vaccine (OPV) has become a major part of the polio problem globally with cVDPV cases exploding in many countries (see sections [1] and [2] above. The call to change vaccines to IPV should be loud and clear. Arguments on the cost of the change should include calculations of the cost of the cases of cVDPV associated disease and the cost of the repeated mop up outbreak control vaccination campaigns. - Mod.MPP]\n\n******\n[4] Cameroon: impact of COVID-19\nDate: Sun 7 Mar 2021 08:24 PM WAT\nSource: Voice of America (VOA) News [edited]\nhttps://www.voanews.com/covid-19-pandemic/cameroon-reports-polio-cases-amid-covid-scare\n\n\nCameroon says 2 polio cases discovered in the capital, Yaounde, 3 weeks ago are a consequence of people refusing to inoculate their children for fear of being infected by COVID-19. The central African state has redeployed health teams to all towns and villages to ask parents to vaccinate their children.\n\nCameroon says it has dispatched health workers to 360 hospitals as part of an awareness campaign against polio. Tetanye Ekoe, president of Cameroon's National Polio Certification Commission, said the awareness teams will teach communities to observe hygiene and to intensify routine immunization, and epidemiological surveillance.\n\nHe said the discovery of 2 type 2 polio cases in Yaounde 3 weeks ago should serve as a wake-up call for people who have turned their backs on polio vaccination. He said it is an illusion to think that the government is hiding behind vaccinations to harm its citizens. Ekoe said he is calling on all Cameroonians to inoculate their children and convince others to take their children to vaccination centers. He said the emergence of polio shows a weak collective immunity. Ekoe said some polio cases may still be undetected because many parents have not been bringing their children to the hospitals out of fear of COVID-19 infection.\n\nCameroon was declared polio-free in 2015, but in 2019, the government of the central African state announced a resurgence on its northern border with Nigeria. The new polio cases were reported in Cameroon in the middle of the 2nd wave of the coronavirus pandemic.\n\nThis month [March 2021] Cameroon's Public Health Ministry reported that the number of people testing positive for COVID-19 had increased from 26 000 to 39 000 between January [2021] and February [2021].\n\nIn December [2020], the government said more than 240 000 children had not received polio vaccines since COVID-19 cases were first reported in Cameroon last March [2020]. The government said parents were refusing to take their children to the hospitals for inoculation because of fear of the coronavirus.\n\nEkoe said rumors last month [February 2021] that the government would secretly vaccinate all Cameroonians against COVID-19 further discouraged people who are scared of the vaccine from visiting hospitals.\n\nPrime minister Joseph Dion Ngute denied in a message Friday [5 Mar 2021] that Cameroon is vaccinating all its citizens who visit hospitals against COVID-19. Ngute said Cameroon is still negotiating to buy a million coronavirus vaccine doses, which will not be administered to people who do not want them. \"Once this vaccine become available, vaccination shall be voluntary,\" he said. \"I would like to note that although vaccination is voluntary and not compulsory, the government encourages all Cameroonians to be vaccinated when the time comes in order to acquire the immunity that will enable our community to protect itself against COVID-19 for a return to normalcy.\"\n\nOn [25 Aug 2020], the World Health Organization announced that wild poliovirus had been eradicated from Africa after 4 consecutive years without any reported cases and massive efforts to immunize children. The WHO said polio-free Africa was a historic moment, moving the world closer to achieving global polio eradication.\n\nThe WHO statement said only Pakistan and Afghanistan continue to see wild poliovirus transmission.\n\nPolio affects mostly young children. Cameroon did not say if the new cases were detected in children or adults.\n\n[byline: Moki Edwin Kindzeka]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Polio vaccination activities are on the list of activities suffering collateral damage as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic. In the early stages of the pandemic, vaccination activities were interrupted, now there is fear on the part of the population that visiting health facilities for vaccination will put them at high risk of transmission of the SARS-CoV-2. CATARINA) MONKEY, SUSPECTED\n***********************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Fri 5 Mar 2021\nSource: Sul Agora [in Portuguese, trans. Mod.TY, edited]\nhttps://sulagora.com.br/saude/sobe-para-40-o-numero-de-macacos-encontrados-mortos-na-regiao-5508\n\n\nIn a little more than 15 days, the region has registered 40 dead monkeys in the cities of Santa Rosa de Lima, Rio Fortuna, Sao Martinho, Grao-Para and Braco do Norte, with 24 in just one week.\n\nTeams from regional Health Surveillance and the Zoonoses Surveillance Unit (UVZ), Tubarao Municipal Health Foundation (FMS), issued an alert about the possibility of yellow fever cases that could be causing the deaths of monkeys in municipalities of the region.\n\nSeveral days ago, 8 dead monkeys were collected that were encountered in the Santa Rosa de Lima region, the results of which still have not been issued. However, the alert was made due to the increase in cases.\n\nAccording to the biologist Sabrina Fernandes Cardoso of the State Health Secretariat, the 1st results of the test are expected at the beginning of next week. \"It is worrisome because there is no apparent cause of death of these animals, with no signs of aggression or accident. In addition to this, the monkeys that were seen constantly by the residents have disappeared,\" she stated.\n\nThe alert has been issued because the appearance of dead monkeys in a given region could indicate the presence of the virus that causes yellow fever. When such an event is detected, the viscera of the animals is taken out and sent for testing in the laboratory in order to confirm, or not, the presence of this virus in these animals, which are considered to be sentinels.\n\n\"The entire locality is being mapped for vaccination coverage of the residents. Epidemiological surveillance teams are visiting house-by-house and orienting the residents. A point to underscore is the increase in vaccination against yellow fever, which is available in all the health posts,\" stated Sabrina, the biologist.\n\nMunicipal residents who by chance encounter a dead monkey are being instructed to go to the nearest health unit to report it. Then, the health team must note the data and communicate it to the Municipal Epidemiological Surveillance, which will take the necessary measures.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-PORT\n<promed-port@promedmail.org>\n\n[The possible (probable) confirmation of yellow fever among the non-human primates under investigation should not be a surprise. On the contrary, it will only confirm the intense circulation of the virus in Santa Catarina, as reported by ProMED-PORT. - Mod.RNA\n\nThe deaths of monkeys in a given area over a short period is characteristic of the sylvan (forest) yellow fever virus transmission cycle. The prompt response of local health authorities to alert the local population to the situation and determine yellow fever vaccination coverage is prudent.\n\nActive transmission of the virus among monkeys carries with it the risk of spillover to humans and ongoing transmission in the urban cycle, which could spread rapidly in a human population with inadequate vaccination coverage. - Mod.TY\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nSanta Catarina, Brazil: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/2975]\nSee Also\nYellow fever - Americas (03): Trinidad & Tobago, monkey die offs 20210226.8216422\nYellow fever - Americas (02): Brazil (PR) monkeys 20210208.8174576\nYellow fever - Americas (01): Brazil (SC) monkey 20210207.8172394\n2020\n---\nYellow fever - Americas (14): Brazil (PR) monkeys 20201227.8050746\nYellow fever - Americas (13): Brazil (PR) monkey 20201211.8010059\nYellow fever - Americas (12): Brazil (PR) monkeys 20201129.7978944\nYellow fever - Americas (06): Brazil, monkey, conservation concern 20200403.7180314\nYellow fever - Americas (03): Brazil, monkey, alert 20200203.6948827\nYellow fever - Americas (02): Brazil, monkey, alert 20200120.6900120\n.................................................rna/sh/ty/msp/sh", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8235916", "headline": "Tomato brown rugose fruit virus - Italy: (SC) spread", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8235916", "date": "2021-03-09 06:10:54", "main_text": "TOMATO BROWN RUGOSE FRUIT VIRUS - ITALY: (SICILY) SPREAD\n********************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Fri 5 Mar 2021\nSource: HortiDaily [edited]\nhttps://www.hortidaily.com/article/9300118/half-of-sicilian-companies-report-tomato-brown-rugose-fruit-virus-infections/\n\n\nA convention discussed the spreading of ToBRFV in Sicily. \"It is important for qualified personnel to perform [the] tests. The virus has already [spread] considerably. Over the past 2 years, we have noticed a lack of communication from companies, as they fear reporting the virus would lead to crops being uprooted,\" explained Professor Walter Davino [University of Palermo].\n\nCurrently, around 45% of companies with protected crops report infections. In Sicily, the problem manifested in 2018. According to Davino, \"no alert was made; no containment measure was implemented; there was no quick and effective detection method. In the meantime, however, we have set up [a] project to identify and track the virus starting from the nurseries.\"\n\nDario Cartabellotta, Regional Council for Agriculture, [said], \"Considering the significant danger of the virus reducing tomato production especially in greenhouses, the Department of Agriculture, with the Plant Protection Service [DA/PPS], [is] monitoring the disease and traces movements of infected seeds and plants. The situation will only get worse until resistant varieties are found. Prevention is the only weapon. The problem was tackled with mandatory phytosanitary measures. In early February 2021, the work was audited by the European Commission. A new national regulation will require additional and complex measures to be implemented.\"\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[_Tomato brown rugose fruit virus_ (ToBRFV) was recently identified as a new member of the genus _Tobamovirus_ (type member _Tobacco mosaic virus_, TMV) in Jordan and soon after in Israel (see links below). Since then, it has also been reported from a number of other countries in Europe and the Mediterranean region, where it appears to be spreading, as well as from North America and China. It was shown to also affect capsicum and has been detected in both plants and seed of both crops. ToBRFV symptoms on tomato vary depending on host cultivar, but they may include chlorosis, mottling, mosaic, and crinkling (rugosis) on leaves; necrotic spots on petioles and calyces; and yellowish mottling, brown spots, and rugosis on fruit, making them unmarketable. On capsicum, leaf symptoms are similar; fruits may be deformed with yellow mottling or green stripes. Almost 100% incidence was reported for some outbreaks in tomato, but not every fruit on an infected plant may show symptoms.\n\nToBRFV (like many tobamoviruses) is seed transmitted and can also be spread by mechanical means, contaminated equipment, as well as with plant or other materials. It is very stable and can remain infectious for months outside a host. Recently, bumblebees, which are used widely as commercial pollinators in glasshouse tomato production, have been shown to be effective vectors of ToBRFV (see link below). Volunteer crop plants and solanaceous weed species are likely pathogen reservoirs. The Tm-22 resistance gene used in some tomato cultivars to protect from other tobamoviruses (such as _Tomato mosaic virus_) does not appear to be effective against ToBRFV. Disease management relies mainly on exclusion but may include phytosanitation (disinfecting tools, removing crop debris) and control of virus reservoirs. Use of certified clean seeds or tomato transplants is crucial. Research on possible seed treatments to eliminate the virus is being carried out (see link below). Tomato seeds are traded widely and are known to pose a risk for spreading viruses and other pathogens internationally (for example, ProMED post 20140122.2222560).\n\nCoinfection of ToBRFV with _Pepino mosaic virus_ (genus _Potexvirus_) and _Tomato spotted wilt virus_ (genus _Orthotospovirus_) have been found (ProMED posts 20191029.6751082, 20200507.7307615). It is thought that the observed symptoms on tomatoes may be due to either virus or to synergism. Further research is needed to clarify a potential role of ToBRFV in coinfections and to determine whether its presence in coinfections may have led to earlier cases of misdiagnosis and delayed identification of this new virus.\n\nMaps\nItaly:\nhttp://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/europe/italy_div96.jpg (with regions)\nEurope, overview:\nhttps://mapofeurope.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/03/europe-political-map.jpg\n\nPictures\nToBRFV symptoms on and\nhttps://www.researchgate.net/publication/321639141/figure/fig2/AS:569722670247937@1512843877331/Tomato-brown-rugose-fruit-virus-ToBRFV-infected-tomato-Solanum-lycopersicum-plants.png\n\nLinks\nAdditional
