"https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8228982", "date": "2021-03-05 09:16:50", "main_text": "CRIMEAN-CONGO HEMORRHAGIC FEVER - ASIA: PAKISTAN (SINDH)\n********************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Mon 1 Mar 2021\nSource: The Nation [edited]\nhttps://nation.com.pk/01-Mar-2021/first-congo-virus-patient-reported-in-karachi\n\n\nA patient at the city's [Karachi] Jinnah Hospital has been diagnosed with Congo virus [Crimean-Congo hemorrhagic fever], citing a hospital official. \"A patient infected with Congo fever virus has been admitted at the Jinnah Hospital,\" Dr Seemi Jamali said today [1 Mar 2021]. It is the 1st patient with the Congo virus reported this year.\n\n\"The patient has been a cowherd and resident of Bilawal Chowrangi in Karachi,\" Dr Jamali said.\n\nThe patient was brought to Jinnah Hospital over symptoms of Congo fever. The hospital confirmed Congo virus in the patient after medical test reports. A Congo virus alert had been issued last year [2020] for the metropolis, stipulating precautionary instructions for all those people who were visiting cattle farms. The alert was issued by the KMC [Karachi Metropolitan Corporation] to hospitals, directing them to adopt special precautions for a Congo-affected patient. It had further asked hospitals to establish special wards for Congo patients, and run awareness campaigns about the virus.\n\nThe disease is caused when a tick attaches itself to the skin of [infected] cattle and when that infected tick or animal comes in contact with people, the highly contagious virus is transmitted into the human body and the person falls ill. The initial symptoms of Congo fever included headache, high fever, rashes, back pain, joint pain, stomach pain, and vomiting.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The CCHF virus is tick-borne and can cause severe viral hemorrhagic fever outbreaks, with a case fatality rate of 10-40 percent. High mortality rates are observed only if there are hemorrhagic manifestations of the disease; up to 80 percent of infections are asymptomatic (https://journals.lww.com/co-infectiousdiseases/Abstract/2007/10000/Crimean_Congo_hemorrhagic_fever.9.aspx, https://www.who.int/news-room/fact-sheets/detail/crimean-congo-haemorrhagic-fever).\n\nThe virus is transmitted by _Hyalomma_ spp. ticks or through contact with infected human blood or animal blood and tissues during and immediately after slaughter.\n\nThe report indicates that there is a history of occupational exposure in this case. The majority of CCHF cases are reported in people involved in the livestock industry, such as agricultural workers, butchers, veterinarians, and on account of exposure in healthcare facilities among healthcare workers who are in contact with suspected CCHF cases.\n\nCCHF cases in Pakistan show biannual peaks, between the months of March-May and August-October. Many factors, including poor sanitation, unhygienic transportation, and numerous animal slaughter sites, inefficient tick-control programs, post-slaughter piles of animal remains, nomadic lifestyle, and lack of general awareness, contribute to the spread of CCHF.\n\nThe health and veterinary (including entomologists/vector control) sectors need to work together on formulating awareness messages to reach the susceptible groups in the general public, especially the high-risk groups, in order to minimize exposures. - Germany: (RP)", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8228894", "date": "2021-03-04 21:29:02", "main_text": "FLAVESCENCE DOREE, GRAPEVINE - GERMANY: (RHINELAND-PALATINATE)\n**************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: February 2021\nSource: European Plant Protection Organisation (EPPO) Reporting Service 02/2021/040 [abridged, edited]\nhttps://gd.eppo.int/reporting/article-6979\n\n\nIn Germany, grapevine flavescence doree phytoplasma (EPPO A2 List) was first recorded in one grapevine plant (_Vitis vinifera_) in 2014 [ProMED-mail post 20141217.3038025] and declared eradicated in 2017 (EPPO RS 2014/202, 2017/135). The NPPO [National Plant Protection Organisation] of Germany informed EPPO that the pathogen was found again at the end of 2020 in one plant (_V. vinifera_) in a vineyard in Rheinland-Pfalz. The identity of the pathogen was confirmed by molecular methods.\n\nDue to the advanced age of the vines, it is excluded that the planting material could be the source of the infestation. It is assumed that the source is an _Alnus_ [alder] stand near the vineyard. The vector _Scaphoideus titanus_ is not present in Germany, but the pathogen may be transmitted from alders to grapevines by cicadas. Official eradication measures will be taken. The whole plot (1 ha, approximatively 3000 plants) will be destroyed. Intensive surveys for flavescence doree and its vectors will be conducted.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Flavescence doree (FD) is one of the most important and destructive diseases of grapevines due to its fast rate of spread within vineyards. The disease was first reported in 1954 in southern France and has been spreading in southern Europe. FD was thought to have been introduced from the United States, the home of its primary vector. It is caused by a phytoplasma (_Candidatus_ Phytoplasma vitis) belonging to the 16SrV (elm yellows) group. Until recently, the only known natural hosts were _Vitis vinifera_ and hybrids, as well as some wild _Vitis_ species as asymptomatic infections.\n\nSymptoms can vary on different grape varieties and usually appear in late spring. They may include shortened internodes, stunting, leaves with downward rolled margins, as well as drooping shoots. Leaves turn yellow in white grape cultivars and red in red ones. Leaf necrosis and bark splitting may also develop; yield is severely reduced, and some vines die, usually in the year following infection. The survivors continue to harbour the pathogen but appear symptomless (latent infections) unless they are re-infected.\n\nFD is spread by the vine leafhopper _Scaphoideus titanus_ and through infected propagation material. Symptomless budwood can carry both eggs of the vector and the pathogen. Reliable diagnosis in both symptomatic and asymptomatic host tissue by molecular methods is vital for disease management, which may include pathogen exclusion, certification of clean propagation material, and removal of infected plants (pathogen reservoirs). Insecticides can reduce vector numbers. The phytoplasma may be eliminated by treating dormant canes with hot water (heat therapy).\n\nIn Europe, a northward spread of the disease is being observed. The vector was reported to have overcome the Alps in the mid 1990s. The 1st report of FD from Germany in 2014 was suspected to have been due to a quarantine incursion from infected Italian rootstocks (ProMED-mail post 20141217.3038025) and was the 1st report of FD north of the Alps. FD has since then also been detected north of the Alps in Switzerland (ProMED-mail post 20190107.6246980) and Austria, where it was also detected in ornamental _Clematis_ species (see link below). The _S. titanus_ vector has been reported in Madeira (see links below) and Russia (ProMED-mail post 20200909.7763574), but so far not the phytoplasma. The spread of FD in central Europe is considered another example of \"warm climate diseases\" moving into cooler regions due to climate change (see, for example, Esca disease of grapevine, ProMED-mail post 20141024.2895414).\n\n\"Eradication\" of pathogens or diseases, particularly once they are established in the field (as had been claimed in Germany for FD above), has hardly ever been successful in the past and should never be relied on as a tool for disease management. Furthermore, proof of absence of a pathogen is principally and practically impossible, because it would require that each and every known or potential host, symptomatic or not, as well as all known and potential vectors or pathogen reservoirs are tested with a method that has a 100% rate of reliability.\n\nMaps\nGermany (with states):\nhttp://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/europe/germany.jpg\nEurope, overview:\nhttp://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/europe/europe_95.jpg\n\nPictures\nFlavescence doree, various grapevine cultivars:\nhttps://bit.ly/2SEcflW,\nhttps://live.staticflickr.com/1478/26546310526_09d79fc749_b.jpg,\nhttps://cdn.unitycms.io/image/ocroped/1200,1200,1000,1000,0,0/9r2R23KvzkM/2a6SZSJsKli9Nwr-fkSvWb.jpg,\nhttps://rebschutzdienst.at/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/Flavescence.jpg and\nhttp://b-c-ing-u.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/2-Vine-leaves-attacked-by-the-Flavescence-Dor%C3%A9e-photo-X.jpg\nFD affected "headline": "African swine fever - Asia (05): China (YN) domestic, spread, pathogenicity", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8228499", "date": "2021-03-04 18:28:28", "main_text": "AFRICAN SWINE FEVER - ASIA (05): CHINA (YUNNAN) DOMESTIC, SPREAD, PATHOGENICITY\n*******************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: Financial Post [abridged, edited]\nhttps://financialpost.com/pmn/business-pmn/china-confirms-swine-fever-in-piglets-in-yunnan-province\n\n\nOn 3 Mar 2021, an outbreak of African swine fever [ASF] has been confirmed in piglets being illegally transported through Funing county in China's southwestern province of Yunnan, the farm ministry said. The case comes amid growing concern that a severe wave of disease in recent months has hit China's hog herd, the world's largest. Six out of the 36 pigs had died, the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Affairs said in a statement late on Tuesday [2 Mar 2021], while 6 more in the truck were sick.\n\nBeijing reports few disease outbreaks on Chinese farms, but some analysts have recently estimated that about 1/5 of the breeding herd in northern China was affected over the winter.\n\nAfrican swine fever is usually fatal to pigs, but recent studies have identified some less lethal variants circulating in China [see comment].\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The information above about the less lethal ASF variants in China has been recently subject to a scientific study published in a Chinese journal (reference below). From the said paper, we introduce the abstract and selected segments from the discussion chapter:\n\n1. Abstract\n\n\"African swine fever virus (ASFV) has been circulating in China for more than 2 years, and it is not clear whether the biological properties of the virus have changed. Here, we report on our surveillance of ASFVs in 7 provinces of China, from June to December 2020. A total of 22 viruses were isolated and characterized as genotype II ASFVs, with mutations, deletions, insertions, or short-fragment replacement occurring in all isolates compared with Pig/HLJ/2018 (HLJ/18), the earliest isolate in China. Eleven isolates had 4 different types of natural mutations or deletion in the EP402R gene and displayed a non-hemadsorbing (non-HAD) phenotype. Four isolates were tested for virulence in pigs; 2 were found to be as highly lethal as HLJ/18. However, 2 non-HAD isolates showed lower virulence but were highly transmissible; infection with 10^6 TCID50 dose was partially lethal and caused acute or sub-acute disease, whereas 10^3 TCID50 dose caused non-lethal, sub-acute or chronic disease, and persistent infection. The emergence of lower virulent natural mutants brings greater difficulty to the early diagnosis of ASF and creates new challenges for ASFV control.\"\n\n2. Discussion (selected segments; for the omitted references, please refer to the full paper)\n\n\"Genotype II ASFV strains, which are endemic in Eastern Europe, Russia, China, and other Southeast Asia regions, mainly exhibit high virulence in pigs, except for isolates Estonia/WB/2014 and Lv17/WB/Rie1. Estonia/WB/2014 was isolated from wild boar in Estonia in 2014 and had a deletion of 14 560 nucleotides at the 5\u2032 end. Animal studies showed that the Estonia/WB/2014 was lethal in wild boar, but did not kill any domestic pigs, although the infected domestic pigs developed disease signs, including lethargy, reduced feed intake, and fever. Lv17/WB/Rie1 was isolated from a hunted wild boar in Latvia in 2017, had a nucleotide deletion at site 395 of its EP402R gene, which caused the loss of expression of CD2v, and had reduced virulence in domestic pigs. In the present study, the 11 non-HAD mutants detected in China have 4 different kinds of genetic changes in the EP402R gene, which all resulted in the deletion of the CD2v protein. Although we only tested and confirmed the partial attenuation of 2 viruses in pigs, it is reasonable to speculate that all of the 11 non-HAD viruses are partially attenuated in pigs. These facts indicate that ASFVs may lose CD2v protein through different strategies during their circulation in pigs, which is probably a compromise of ASFVs to the host's antiviral response, but the underlying mechanism is still unclear.\n\n\"Currently, there are no commercial vaccines or specific treatments available for ASF. Therefore, control of the disease relies on the rapid diagnosis and culling of infected animals. The emergence of the non-HAD mutants will cause more problems and pose bigger challenge for the ASF control in China since they cause a much more delayed course, and mild, chronic disease signs, while being continuously shed via the oral and rectal routes. Recently, we developed a safe and efficient 7-gene-deleted live vaccine (HLJ/18-7GD) based on HLJ/18. The protective efficacy of the HLJ/18-7GD vaccine against these newly emerged, lower virulent strains need to be urgently evaluated.\"\n\nOn top of ASF, which reportedly started its circulation in China in August 2018, China's livestock industry has been plagued by 2 other recently introduced viral diseases that are high on OIE's list of transboundary animal diseases, namely lumpy skin disease in cattle and PPR [peste des petits ruminants] in small ruminants (sheep and goats). Fortunately, and in difference with ASF, potent vaccines against these 2 diseases are commercially available.\n\nReference:\n\nEncheng Sun, Zhenjiang Zhang, Zilong Wang, Xijun He, et al.: Emergence and prevalence of naturally occurring lower virulent African swine fever viruses in domestic pigs in China in 2020. Science China Life Sciences. 2021; doi: https://doi.org/10.1007/s11427-021-1904-4.\n\n- Mod.AS\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nFuning Xian, Yunnan, China: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/68214]\nSee Also\nAfrican swine fever - Asia (03): China (Hong Kong) domestic, OIE 20210209.8179230\nAfrican swine fever - Asia (01): China, domestic, illicit vaccine susp 20210122.8126032\n2018\n----\nAfrican swine fever - Asia (14): China (JL) domestic swine, spread, OIE 20180921.6044224\nAfrican swine fever - Asia (10): China (AH) domestic swine, spread 20180830.5997998\nAfrican swine fever - Asia: China (LN) domestic swine, 1st report, OIE 20180803.5945484\n.................................................sb/arn/tw/lxl", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8227406", "headline": "COVID-19 update (86): transmission, variants, immune profiling, WHO, global", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8227406", "date": "2021-03-04 15:17:04", "main_text": "CORONAVIRUS DISEASE 2019 UPDATE (86): TRANSMISSION, VARIANTS, SYMPTOMS, IMMUNE PROFILING, WHO, GLOBAL\n*****************************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nIn this update:\n[1] South Korea: geospatial analysis of age-specific SARS-CoV-2 transmission patterns\n[2] Variants & immunity\n[3] Prevalence of COVID-19-related symptoms by age group\n[4] Immune profiling in COVID-19 patients\n[5] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 3 Mar 2021)\n[6] Global update: Worldometer accessed 3 Mar 2021 18:25 EST (GMT-5)\n\n******\n[1] South Korea: geospatial analysis of age-specific SARS-CoV-2 transmission patterns\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: LitCovid [edited]\nhttps://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/research/coronavirus/publication/33650338\n\n\nref: Yi S, Kim YM, Choe YJ, et al. Geospatial analysis of age-specific SARS-CoV-2 transmission patterns in households, Korea. J Korean Med Sci. 2021 Mar 1;36(8):e63. doi: 10.3346/jkms.2021.36.e63. PMID: 33650338; PMCID: PMC7921369\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nAbstract\n--------\nWe constructed an age-to-age infection matrix to characterize the household transmission pattern of coronavirus disease 2019 (COVID-19) in Korea. Among 4048 household clusters, within-age group infection dominated the overall household transmissions. Transmission of severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus-2 was more common from adults to children than from children to adults.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED Rapporteur Kunihiko Iizuka\n\n[According to this study, household transmission occurred in 21% of the cases; with one index case infecting an average of 1.57 household members. Transmission of severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2 (SARS-CoV-2) was more common from adults to children than from children to adults https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/32634405/. This underscores the importance of additional awareness targeting the adult population and reappraises the implication of school closure on SARS-CoV-2 transmission in the households. - Mod.UBA]\n\n******\n[2] Variants & immunity\n[A] Brazil\nDate: Tue 2 Mar 2021 10.09 AM EST\nSource: The Guardian [edited]\nhttps://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/mar/02/brazil-variant-evaded-immunity-previous-covid-cases\n\n\nThe coronavirus variant originally found in Manaus in Brazil and detected in 6 cases in the UK was able to infect 25% to 61% of the people in the Amazonian city who might have expected to be immune after a 1st bout of Covid, researchers say.\n\nThe extent to which P1 can evade the immune system, and potentially vaccines, emerged as the UK health secretary said the hunt for one person who tested positive for P1 - but did not leave contact details - had narrowed to 379 households in the south-east of England.\n\nMatt Hancock said 5 people had quarantined at home. The 6th took a home test but did not fill in the necessary form. \"Incidents like this are rare and only occur in around 0.1% of tests,\" he told MPs in the House of Commons. \"We've identified the batch of home test kits in question, our search has narrowed from the whole country down to 379 households in the south-east of England and we're contacting each one.\"\n\nHancock also said that a 3rd vaccine might be necessary in the autumn, against P1 and similar variants such as B1351, which was 1st detected in South Africa. Both have mutations in the spike protein that can help virus variants escape the current vaccines.\n\n\"Our current vaccines have not yet been studied against this variant and we're working to understand what impact it might have, but we do know that this variant has caused significant challenges in Brazil, so we're doing all we can to stop the spread of this new variant in the UK, to analyse its effects and to develop an updated vaccine that works on all these variants of concern and protect the progress that we've made as a nation,\" said Hancock.\n\nThe international team of scientists that detected P1 in Manaus is calling for more genetic sequencing of emerging variants around the world, saying that only with knowledge of how Sars-Cov2 is mutating can the pandemic be brought under control.\n\nThe variant, called P1, not only has potential to evade the immune protection of previous illness or vaccines, but is more transmissible than the original coronavirus. The study in Manaus, which has not yet been published in peer-reviewed form, found it was about 1.4 to 2.2 times more transmissible than the original virus.\n\nThe scientists said at a briefing that 6 cases, detected promptly in the UK, did not presage a significant spread of the variant. It was vital, however, to identify variants emerging throughout the world in countries that had little or no genomic sequencing capacity at the moment, they said.\n\nThe research was carried out by the Brazil-UK Cadde project, whose work on genetic sequencing predates the pandemic. It includes the Institute of Tropical Medicine in Sao Paulo, the London School of Hygiene and Tropical Medicine and universities in Oxford, London and Birmingham.\n\nManaus, the largest city in the Amazon basin, suffered a 1st wave of Covid in April/May [2020]. Studies of blood donors suggested 66% of people had antibodies against the virus in July [2020] and 76% by October [2020], which would have been expected to give them immunity. But the city suffered a serious 2nd wave. There could have been various explanations, including the possibility that the data on previous infection was wrong, but the team of researchers identified the P1 variant on [6 Dec 2020]. It spread rapidly: within 8 weeks, it was implicated in 87% of cases.\n\nDr. Nuno Faria of the MRC Centre for Global Infectious Disease Analysis at Imperial College London, said it had concluded that the variant was causing people who had already suffered from Covid to get it again. \"If 100 people were infected in Manaus last year [2020], somewhere between 25 and 61 of them are susceptible to reinfection by P1,\" he said at a briefing. \"We caution, however, that our results from analysis should not be generalised to other epidemiological contexts and/or other variants of concern.\"\n\nProf. Sharon Peacock, the director of Cog-UK, the consortium responsible for the genomic sequencing of the virus and its variants, said P1 has spread to 25 countries to date. \"It is being distributed around the world. But I would say that in terms of the UK, we have just 6 cases identified, which we heard about yesterday [Mon 1 Mar 2021] from Public Health England, and from the government,\" she said.\n\nPeacock expressed a note of caution about the findings from Manaus. \"We need to see whether this is generalisable to other settings, she said. \"So I think it would be wise to indicate that this is relevant to where the study was done, but we don't know how that will pan out in other countries, including the UK.\n\n\"The response that we've taken in the UK has been very brisk, and is appropriate, but very vigorous.\" Public Health England was investigating the 6 known cases of people infected with P1, tracing contacts and taking appropriate action, she said.\n\nThe research shows that P1 has 17 mutations and many are similar to those found in the spike protein of the variant found in South Africa, called B1351. In particular, a mutation called E484K that they share appears to enable the variants to escape the immune system, which means that vaccines may have reduced efficacy.\n\n[Byline: Sarah Boseley]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED Rapporteur Kunihiko Iizuka\n\n[Also review; Genomics and epidemiology of a novel SARS-CoV-2 lineage in Manaus, Brazil https://raw.githubusercontent.com/CADDE-CENTRE/Novel-SARS-CoV-2-P1-Lineage-in-Brazil/main/manuscript/FINAL_P1_MANUSCRIPT_25-02-2021_combined.pdf. - Mod.UBA]\n\n----\n[B] South Africa\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: Reuters [edited]\nhttps://jp.reuters.com/article/uk-health-coronavirus-safrica/south-african-scientists-find-antibodies-from-variant-may-offer-cross-protection-idUSKCN2AV1SK\n\n\nResearch by South African scientists suggests that antibodies triggered by exposure to the country's dominant coronavirus variant can prevent infection by other variants, the scientists said on [Wed 3 Mar 2021].\n\nThe findings in laboratory studies offer hope that COVID-19 vaccines based on the 501Y.V2 variant 1st identified late last year [2020] could protect against multiple variants circulating in different parts of the world.\n\nThe more contagious variant drove a 2nd wave of infections in South Africa that peaked in January [2021] and is believed to have spread to many other countries in Africa and other continents.\n\n\"We used plasma ... from people that were infected in this latest wave with the 501Y.V2 and we used it against the 1st-wave virus, ... what we found is that it could neutralise, OK not as well as it could neutralise itself but it's not bad at all,\" Alex Sigal from the Africa Health Research Institute told a news conference. Sigal said vaccines designed with the 501Y.V2 variant in mind \"might be cross-protective to other variants, ... this gives you some idea how this problem of variants can be solved\".\n\nPenny Moore, a professor at the National Institute for Communicable Diseases, said the antibody response from the 501Y.V2 variant was only reduced 3-fold against the 1st-wave virus, whereas the response from the 1st-wave virus was reduced 9-fold against 501Y.V2.\n\n\"It's not that the antibodies that are triggered by 501Y.V2 are somehow magical, there is a drop-off, ... but unlike the antibodies triggered by the original variant they seem to somehow have a little bit more breadth,\" she told the same briefing.\n\nSalim Abdool Karim, a top government adviser on COVID-19, said major vaccine manufacturers including Pfizer, AstraZeneca and Johnson & Johnson were already making vaccines based on the 501Y.V2 variant. Moderna had already adapted its shot and was putting it into human studies, he added.\n\nHe predicted that by the end of 2021 most vaccine manufacturers would have adapted their shots, \"not because they are specifically worrying about the virus coming from South Africa ... but because key mutations in the 501Y.V2 are actually also present in many other variants.\"\n\nHealth Minister Zweli Mkhize said the research was encouraging and that genomics surveillance had helped the government respond to the pandemic.\n\nSouth Africa has recorded by far the most COVID-19 infections and deaths on the African continent, at 1.5 million cases and over 50 000 fatalities to date.\n\n[Byline: Alexander Winning]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED Rapporteur Kunihiko Iizuka\n\n[Also review; Escape of SARS-CoV-2 501Y.V2 variants from neutralization by convalescent plasma\nhttps://www.ahri.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/MEDRXIV-2021-250224v1-Sigal.pdf - Mod.UBA]\n\n******\n[3] Prevalence of COVID-19-related symptoms by age group\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: LitCovid [edited]\nhttps://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/research/coronavirus/publication/33650071\n\n\nref: Unim B, Palmieri L, Lo Noce C, Brusaferro, S and Onder, G. Prevalence of COVID-19-related symptoms by age group. Aging Clin Exp Res. 2021 Mar 1:1-3. doi: 10.1007/s40520-021-01809-y. Epub ahead of print. PMID: 33650071; PMCID: PMC7919615.\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nAbstract\n--------\nBackground\nSevere acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus-2 has caused over 95 million confirmed cases of COVID-19 and over 2 million deaths worldwide. According to current literature data, older adults have higher risk of severe disease and mortality due to COVID-19. It is also known that older adults often do not present typical symptoms of diseases. The aim of the study was to assess if the prevalence of typical COVID-19-related symptoms varies by age group.\n\nMethods\nMedical charts of a random sample of COVID-19 patients dying in-hospital were retrieved through an integrated national surveillance system and reviewed by a group of researchers at the Italian National Institute of Health. Detailed information on COVID-19-related symptoms were extracted and analyzed.\n\nResults\nA total of 3241 confirmed cases of COVID-19-related deaths were identified from 4391 reviewed medical charts. The mean number of COVID-19-related symptoms progressively declined with age, from 2.1 in patients aged under 60 years to 1.7 in those aged 90 years or older (p < 0.001). Moreover, fever, cough, and diarrhea significantly declined with increasing age.\n\nConclusions\nOlder adults have atypical presentation of symptoms and may be paucisymptomatic. This may lead to a diagnostic and therapeutic delay which aggravates the prognosis of COVID-19. Special attention should be posed when assessing individuals aged 65 years and older with suspected COVID-19.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n[4] Immune profiling in COVID-19 patients\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: LitCovid [edited]\nhttps://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/research/coronavirus/publication/33648924\n\n\nref: Schrijver B, Assmann JLJC, van Gammeren AJ, et al. Extensive longitudinal immune profiling reveals sustained innate immune activation in COVID-19 patients with unfavorable outcome. Eur Cytokine Netw. 2020 Dec 1; 31(4): 154-167. doi: 10.1684/ecn.2020.0456. PMID: 33648924\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nAbstract\n--------\nCOVID-19 differs substantially between individuals, ranging from mild to severe or even fatal. Heterogeneity in the immune response against SARS-COV-2 likely contributes to this. Therefore, we explored the temporal dynamics of key cellular and soluble mediators of innate and adaptive immune activation in relation to COVID-19 severity and progression. A total of 44 patients with a PCR-proven diagnosis of COVID-19 were included. Extensive cellular (leukocytes and T-lymphocyte subsets) and serological immune profiling (cytokines, soluble cell surface molecules, and SARS-CoV-2 antibodies) was performed at hospital admission and every 3-4 days during hospitalization. Measurements and disease outcome were compared between patients with an unfavorable (IC admission and/or death) and favorable (all others) outcome. Patients with an unfavorable outcome had higher leukocyte numbers at baseline, mostly due to increased neutrophils, whereas lymphocyte and monocyte numbers were reduced. CRP, IL-6, CCL2, CXCL10, and GM-CSF levels were higher at baseline in the unfavorable group, whereas IL-7 levels were lower. SARS-CoV-2 antibodies were more frequently absent in the unfavorable group. Longitudinal analysis revealed delayed kinetics of activated CD4 and CD8 T-lymphocyte subsets in the unfavorable group. Furthermore, whereas CRP, IL-6, CXCL10, and GM-CSF declined in the favorable group, these cytokines declined with delayed kinetics, remained increased, or even increased further in the unfavorable group. Our data indicate a state of increased innate immune activation in COVID19-patients with an unfavorable outcome at hospital admission, which remained over time, as compared with patients with a favorable outcome.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n[5] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 3 Mar 2021)\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: WHO [abridged, edited]\nhttps://covid19.who.int/table\n\n\n*Daily case reports as of 3 Mar 2021 16:18 CET\n\nSurveillance\n------------\nWHO region (no. countries/territories):\nTotal confirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nWestern Pacific Region (19): 1 636 896 (5059) / 29 244 (111)\nEuropean Region (61): 39 038 341 (167 303) / 871 340 (3645)\nSouth East Asia Region (10): 13 581 219 (21 861) / 208 893 (305)\nEastern Mediterranean Region (22): 6 482 557 (33 299) / 145 666 (398)\nRegion of the Americas (54): 50 824 766 (114 932) / 1 215 955 (3090)\nAfrican Region (49): 2 863 687 (5827) / 72 644 (267)\nCases on an international conveyance (Diamond Princess): 745 (0) / 13 (0)\n\nConfirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\nGrand total: 114 428 211 (348 281) / 2 543 755 (7807)\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Data by country, area, or territory for 3 Mar 2021 can be accessed at https://promedmail.org/wp-content/uploads/world-pdf/2021%20WHO%20Daily%20Tables%20Mar3_1614861430.pdf.\n\n- The Americas region reported 33% of daily case numbers and 39.6% of the daily deaths reported in the past 24 hours and maintained its position as the most severely affected region, having reported more than 50.82 million cases. Seroprevalence studies indicate CCPP presence in West Africa (though no sites in Morocco were evaluated). Given the OIE regulation of CCPP it is an important rule out.\n\n--\nCommunicated by\nMay Meghan\nUniversity of New England\nPortland, ME, USA\n<mmay3@une.edu>\n\n[CCPP is a severe disease of goats occurring in many countries in Africa and Asia; synonyms include pleuropneumonie contagieuse caprine (France), bou-frida (Algeria), and abu-nini (Sudan).\n\nPeracute, acute and chronic forms occur in endemic areas. In case of the peracute presentation, the affected goats may die within 1-3 days with minimal clinical signs. Diagnosis is carried out by clinical and necropsy observations that should be confirmed by laboratory tests. Post-mortem examination reveals fibrinous pleuropneumonia with massive lung hepatisation and pleurisy, accompanied by accumulation of straw coloured pleural fluid. CCPP is strictly a respiratory disease. One wonders if necropsies were undertaken in the event described. An OIE disease card (etiology, epidemiology, diagnosis, prevention & control) is available at https://www.oie.int/fileadmin/Home/eng/Animal_Health_in_the_World/docs/pdf/Disease_cards/CONTAGIOUS_CAPRINE_PLEURO.pdf.\n\nAccording to the Moroccan daily Istitmar dated 28 Feb 2021, the 1st mortalities (n=47) of this event were recorded in the night of Tue 23 and Wed 24 Feb 2021. The location was visited on Sun 28 Feb 2021 by a team composed of local authorities, gendarmerie, and a veterinarian; no evidence of the cause of the (apparently, sudden) death could be found. See (in Arabic, including picture) at https://cutt.ly/tl3KTYl. - Mods.SF/AS\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map of Morocco: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/30671]\nSee Also\nUndiagnosed deaths, goat - Morocco: (SS) RFI 20210303.8225738\n.................................................arn/sf/mj/lxl", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8226934", "headline": "Ebola update (22): Congo DR (NK) Guinea, WHO", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8226934", "date": "2021-03-04 09:04:40", "main_text": "EBOLA UPDATE (22): DEMOCRATIC REPUBLIC OF CONGO (NORTH KIVU) GUINEA, WHO\n************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nIn this update:\n[1] WHO/AFRO: cooperative effort among Guinea neighbors\n[2] Traditional healers\n[3] Congo DR (North Kivu): 2 individuals cured\n\n******\n[1] WHO/AFRO: cooperative effort among Guinea neighbors\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: WHO/AFRO [edited]\nhttps://www.afro.who.int/news/west-african-health-ministers-joint-fight-against-ebola\n\n\nWest African health ministers in joint fight against Ebola\n----------------------------------------------------------\nMinisters of Health from Guinea -- which is combating a new Ebola outbreak -- and neighbouring countries have agreed on a unified front to combat the virus that re-emerged about 3 weeks ago.\n\nThe meeting was opened by His Excellency, the Prime Minister of Guinea, Dr Ibrahima Kassory Fofana in Guinea's capital, Conakry on [2 Mar 2021]. Ministers and government representatives from Cote d'Ivoire, Guinea-Bissau, Liberia, Mali, Senegal, and Sierra Leone attended the inter-ministerial meeting.\n\n\"If in 2014 Guinea and the neighbouring countries were victims of Ebola, this time around Guinea and the region are resolutely facing up to Ebola,\" said H.E. the Prime Minister.\n\nThe ministers agreed in a final declaration to set up a coordination mechanism, enhance cross-border collaboration, including working with communities, to support the efforts in containing the virus. They also agreed to facilitate import regulations for vaccines and drugs as well as promote measures that were effective in bringing the 2014-2016 Ebola outbreak in West Africa under control.\n\nGuinea declared an outbreak on [14 Feb 2021] after cases were confirmed positive for Ebola in a rural community in N'Zerekore prefecture, which lies near the border with Cote d'Ivoire and Liberia. As of [2 Mar 2021], 17 cases (13 confirmed, 4 probable) had been reported.\n\n\"We are greatly encouraged by the common front taken by Guinea's neighbours to tackle this outbreak. We know from experience how much this is critical in fighting Ebola,\" said Dr Abdou Salam Gueye, Regional Emergency Director at the World Health Organization (WHO) Regional Office for Africa. \"With close cross-border trade and social ties, we cannot ignore the importance of regional approaches against health crises.\"\n\nIn support of Guinea's health authorities, WHO and partner organizations have ramped up response to the outbreak. Ebola vaccinations were launched just 9 days after the outbreak was declared. To date, 1317 people have been vaccinated and 32 000 vaccine doses have so far been delivered.\n\nAll the 6 countries bordering Guinea are stepping up readiness. Surveillance and screening are being stepped up at border crossing points and in high-risk communities. Rapid response teams are being deployed to border areas to support the preparedness plans of health districts. Testing and treatment facilities are being scaled up and work to ensure communities take full ownership and rally around public health responses is underway.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n******\n[2] Traditional healers\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021 09:41 WAT\nSource: Radio Okapi [in French, machine trans., edited]\nhttps://www.afro.who.int/news/west-african-health-ministers-joint-fight-against-ebola\n\n\nNorth Kivu: Provincial Minister of Health calls on traditional healers to get involved in the fight against Ebola\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nThe Provincial Minister of Health, Dr Nzanzu Salita, invites traditional healers to get involved in the fight against the 12th Ebola epidemic. He made this call on Tuesday [2 Mar 2021], during an exchange he had with them. According to the minister, during the epidemic period, some patients flee conventional structures to seek treatment from traditional healers.\n\n\"This is why we wanted to sound the alarm among traditional healers to be vigilant, especially since we have all been trained in integrated disease surveillance and response so that they can help us alert patients who show signs resembling Ebola and COVID-19. They understood the magnitude of the threat and promised to lend us a hand,\" said Dr Nzanzu Salita.\n\nExpressing their commitment to the fight against Ebola and COVID-19, these traditional healers pleaded for the provision of personal protective equipment, in order to protect themselves against Ebola in their various centers.\n\nThe provincial health minister has promised to find a solution to this request in the near future.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n\n[Bringing the traditional healers into the response to combat Ebola would be very helpful. But they are at high risk of infection when treating infected patients. If they could be provided with personal protective equipment, they would be less likely to become infected themselves and thus unlikely to transmit the disease to naive individuals who come to seek care or accompany those who do. - Mod.LK]\n\n******\n[3] Congo DR (North Kivu): 2 individuals cured\nDate: Wed 3 Mar 2021\nSource: Media Congo.net on Twitter [in French, machine trans., edited]\nhttps://mobile.twitter.com/mediacongo/status/1367169904886054912\n\n\n#Butembo [North Kivu]: 2 people cured of Ebola virus disease officially left the Ebola treatment center on Wednesday [3 Mar 2021]. 11 cases have already been notified, with 4 deaths\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n\n[Seeing individuals released from treatment centers after recovering from Ebola is always a cause for celebration. [edited]\nhttp://outbreaknewstoday.com/1st-human-dirofilariasis-case-reported-in-ukraine-this-year-90740/\n\n\nOfficials in the southeastern Ukraine city of Melitopol are reporting the 1st human case of dirofilariasis this past January [2021]. The individual was confirmed as having dirofilariasis of the eyelid.\n\nThere have been 200 cases reported in Ukraine in the past 2 decades.\n\nExperts say that in recent years, there has been an increase in the incidence of dirofilariasis in those countries where it is considered rare. You can protect yourself only by preventing mosquito bites.\n\nThe definitive treatment of dirofilaria infection in humans is surgical removal of lung granulomas and nodules under the skin; this treatment is also curative.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Human infection with _D. repens_ is well known in the Russia Federation and the countries previously part of the Soviet Union.\n\nA recent review included data from 236 human patients (Ermakova LA, Nagorny SA, Krivorotova EY, Pshenichnaya NY, Matina ON. _Dirofilaria repens_ in the Russian Federation: current epidemiology, diagnosis, and treatment from a federal reference center perspective. Heartworm on the rise - new insights into _Dirofilaria immitis_ epidemiology. Parasitol Res. 2018 Jul;117(7):2347-2350. doi: 10.1007/s00436-018-5912-9.\n- Blaizot R et al. It might lead to heavy loss if the disease is not checked from spreading further. Observers claimed that leaf blight disease happens due to fungal infection and advised to use pesticide with constraint. They also advised to conduct awareness programme to sensitise the farmers about the disease.\n\nHowever, the [local] agriculture department has failed to be of any help. The farmers are also not seeking the assistance of farm experts to contain the disease. They are buying pesticide from the market. As a result, wrong use of pesticide results in crop loss and reduced output.\n\n[A] scientist at the Krishi Vigyan Kendra [agricultural extension centre] in Jajpur said that the disease has affected the crop as the farmers do not treat the seeds before cultivation. He advised farmers to treat seeds and contact the agriculture scientist before making use of pesticide on their crops.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[A number of tomato diseases have been reported from the region; many of them can also affect potatoes and other solanaceous crops. Leaf blight symptoms, as mentioned above, can be due to a number of mainly fungal and bacterial pathogens. For example, late blight of tomato and potato (caused by the fungus-like organism _Phytophthora infestans_) is rife in the region, with a severe strain spreading there (ProMED-mail post 20180418.5755980). It is not clear whether this disease has been excluded as a possibility.\n\nThe problems above may also be due to a combination of pathogens and/or other factors. Reliable molecular diagnosis of any pathogen(s) involved will be needed in order to be able to design suitable management strategies for the farmers. However, the recommendation above to make use of seed treatments and expert advice in the meantime is certainly sound.\n\nMaps\nIndia (with states):\nhttp://www.mapsofindia.com/maps/india/india-political-map.htm\nOdisha districts:\nhttps://www.mapsofindia.com/maps/orissa/orissa.htm\n\nPictures\nSymptoms of some tomato diseases via:\nhttp://www.ipmimages.org/browse/AreaSubs.cfm?area=63\n\nLinks\nList of major diseases and pathogens of tomato:\nhttps://www.apsnet.org/edcenter/resources/commonnames/Pages/Tomato.aspx\nFact sheets of some major tomato diseases via:\nhttp://vegetablemdonline.ppath.cornell.edu/factsheets/Tomato_List.htm\n- Mod.DHA]\nSee Also\n2020\n----\nUndiagnosed disease, tomato - New Zealand: spread by sheep", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8225848", "date": "2021-03-03 18:13:55", "main_text": "THEILERIA - NEW ZEALAND: SPREAD BY SHEEP\n****************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Mon 22 Feb 2021 21:45 NZDT\nSource: New Zealand Herald [abridged, edited]\nhttps://www.nzherald.co.nz/the-country/news/research-shows-sheep-may-help-spread-bovine-anaemia-parasite/CYVYYW6ZPT35XXN2TXOKRSWQLY/\n\n\nNew Zealand researchers have proven sheep can carry and potentially spread the parasite behind the bovine anaemia epidemic. Sheep were asymptomatic carriers of the tick-borne parasite _Theileria orientalis_, which meant they were unaffected by the disease but could spread it to the ticks feeding on them.\n\n_T. orientalis_ is a tickborne intracellular parasite of red blood cells causing severe and mild infections in various ruminants worldwide. To date [22 Feb 2021], there have been 11 types identified within this species, of which 4 types are presently found in New Zealand cattle, researchers said.\n\nSince 2012, New Zealand suffered a substantial epidemic of infectious bovine anaemia in both dairy and beef cattle associated with the Ikeda type. Researchers believed the speed at which the disease spread through the North Island suggested other species could have been involved in transmission.\n\nTherefore, the aim of a series of related experiments was to test the null hypothesis sheep can't maintain _T. orientalis_ Ikeda-type infection or infect ticks feeding on them. Several studies were conducted over 2 years to address this hypothesis.\n\nThe studies showed sheep can have detectable levels of _T. orientalis_ Ikeda-type infection, in both the acute and chronic phase, and _Haemaphysalis longicornis_ (also known as the Asian longhorned tick) larvae can become infected when feeding on sheep. Researchers recorded no anaemia, weight loss, or clinical disease in the sheep in the acute phase of infection.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Some North Island, as well as South Island, cattle are suffering anemia as the result of infection with a strain of the parasite _Theileria orientalis_, called Ikeda. The infection is spread by ticks.\n\n\"The intracellular protozoal parasite _Theileria orientalis_ ikeda has rapidly spread across southeastern Australia since 2006, causing deaths and production losses in cattle. The 3-host \"bush tick\" _Haemaphysalis longicornis_ (Neumann) appears the principal biological vector in the endemic regions. To generate sufficient numbers of ticks to produce stabilate for infection to confirm vector competency and for acaricide trials, the optimal conditions and stage-specific intervals for the generational lifecycle of _H. longicornis_ was defined on 2 dogs and 2 steers. To determine whether _H. longicornis_ was a definitive host for _T. orientalis_, nymphal stages were fed on a steer infected with _T. orientalis_ and moulted adults were permitted to feed for 3 days on an uninfected calf prior to harvest. Subsequent detection of infection after inoculation of 4 naive calves with stabilate produced from ground-up adult ticks or dissected salivary glands confirmed _H. longicornis_ as one final (definitive) host for _T. orientalis_ in Australia.\" (Source: https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2590138919300189).\n\nNow it seems we know this particular tick feeds on sheep with no ill effects to the sheep.\n\nThe issue first appeared in Northland in August 2012, and since then cases were found across the North Island but predominantly in the upper island. The bulk of cases appear in areas where ticks are very prevalent. It appears tick populations increased rapidly as a result of summer's drought [in 2013], and the mild winter might mean they survived and became active early during the 2014 season.\n\nIt now appears the sheep may be harboring the infective agent and passing it to the ticks. While this is great research, it is in some ways disheartening to realize the sheep may be the source of the situation. It seems keeping cattle and sheep treated with a tick control will be essential to the health of cattle. - Mod.TG\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nNew Zealand: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/164]\nSee Also\n2015\n----\nTheileria, bovine - Australia, New Zealand: background 20151205.3841381\n2014\n----\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand (04): (South Island) 20141125.2987470\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand (03): (South Island) 20141108.2938293\nTheileria, bovine - Australia (02): (SA) 20141018.2876525\nTheileria, bovine - Australia: (VI) 20140823.2715493\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand (02) 20140621.2557021\nTheileria, cervid - China: (northwest) 20140516.2477057\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand 20140423.2422975\n2013\n----\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand (03) 20131123.2069997\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand (02) 20130925.1966132\nTheileria, bovine - New Zealand 20130922.1960608\nTheileria, bovine - Australia (02) 20130613.1769991\nTheileria, bovine - Australia 20130612.1768157\n2012\n----\nTheileria, bovine - Australia (03): (VI) 20120605.1156373\nTheileria, bovine - Australia (02): (VI) 20120604.1155307\nTheileria, bovine - Australia: (NS) 20120325.1080410\n.................................................sb/tg/rd/lxl", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8225738", "headline": "Undiagnosed deaths, goat - Morocco: (SS) RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8225738", "date": "2021-03-03 14:05:51", "main_text": "UNDIAGNOSED DEATHS, GOAT - MOROCCO: (SOUSS-MASSA) REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n*************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Tue 2 Mar 2021\nSource: Hespress [in Arabic, trans. Mod.SF, edited]\nhttps://cutt.ly/slMC697\n\n\nMore than 200 goats have died in the village \"Torrit Ekarkaren\" from Targua n'touchka in Chtouka Ait Baha province, over the past few days and the reasons are still unknown.\n\nAccording to the owner of the dead herd, the incident caused a financial, environmental, and sanitary disaster.
