Spain: susp. international trade issue, RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8221811", "date": "2021-03-01 20:30:53", "main_text": "BLUETONGUE, CATTLE - SPAIN: SUSPECTED, INTERNATIONAL TRADE ISSUE, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n*****************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: 1 Mar 2021\nSource: The Guardian [edited]\nhttps://www.theguardian.com/environment/2021/mar/01/cattle-stranded-on-ship-to-be-destroyed-in-port-as-second-vessel-returns-to-spain\n\n\nSpanish authorities are about to begin slaughtering hundreds of calves that have spent months crisscrossing the Mediterranean, said a lawyer for the cattle shippers.\n\nThe 864 cattle due for slaughter are onboard the Karim Allah, which is docked in the Spanish port of Cartagena. It is one of 2 vessels that left Spain in mid-December 2020 to deliver live cargoes of young bulls. The 2nd vessel, Elbeik, loaded almost 1800 cattle from Tarragona.\n\nThe Elbeik, now carrying more than 1700 cattle, also appears to be returning to Spain.\n\nBoth shipments ran into problems when they were refused entry by various countries, including Turkey and Libya, owing to fears the animals had a disease called bluetongue, which causes lameness and hemorrhaging among cattle but does not affect humans.\n\nDisease regulations outlined by Spanish officials mean the cattle cannot re-enter the EU having attempted to enter Libya. The slaughter order issued to Karim Allah's management, seen by the Guardian, states that Libya: \"Has a ban on the export of animals to the EU due to the existence of, among other epizootic diseases of major impact for livestock, foot-and-mouth disease in that state\" [see comment].\n\n\"The Spanish authorities have indicated they will start killing the cattle on Tue [2 Mar 2021],\" said Miquel Masramon, a lawyer representing Talia Shipping Line. The Karim Allah is owned by Khalifeh Livestock Trading and managed by Talia Shipping Line, both based in Lebanon, while the cattle are owned by a 3rd party.\n\nIn a statement on Saturday [27 Feb 2021], the agriculture ministry indicated that if the Karim Allah did not begin to \"isolate and slaughter the animals in accordance with the applicable regulations\" the ministry would do so.\n\nA source at the ministry said on Sun [28 Feb 2021] the shipper had been informed that it had until Mon 1 Mar 2021 midday to begin the slaughter. The ministry said: \"It is up to the shipowner in the 1st instance to isolate and slaughter the animals. He has until 1st thing tomorrow morning [Mon 1 Mar 2021] to communicate his decision to the administration.\"\n\nBoth the director of Talia Shipping Line, Majed Eid, and Masramon said they would fight the decision. Their aim, they say, is to allow the cattle time to heal and then find a new buyer, once they have the results of bluetongue blood tests taken last week.\n\nA report by Spanish veterinary officials who boarded the Karim Allah last week said the captain told them of 22 deaths at sea. Another 9 cattle were not accounted for. The report said 20 of the animals that died were chopped up and thrown overboard during the journey, citing information provided by the captain.\n\nThe report concluded that the animals had suffered from the lengthy journey and were generally in a poor state. Some were unwell and not fit for transport outside the EU, or fit to be allowed into Europe. Euthanasia would be best for their health and welfare, it concluded.\n\nThe report did not say whether the cattle had bluetongue but noted other skin, eye and leg conditions including alopecia, flaking, scabs, and joint inflammation compatible with septic arthritis.\n\nOn Sunday [28 Feb 2021], Masramon said he was trying to get a new veterinary report and was hoping to get a vet to board the ship and \"inspect the animals and respond to the Spanish authorities' veterinary report. The problem right now is to get the [vet] official approval to enter the port.\"\n\n[Byline: Sophie Kevany & Ashifa Kassam]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Following the refusal to unload its cargo in Turkey, the Karim Allah visited Tripoli (Libya) in an attempt to sell the Spanish cattle there, but was similarly refused. Spain's refusal to allow the unloading of the returning cattle is attributed by the authorities to the passage of the vessel in Tripoli, since Libya is regarded FMD-infected. Vaccination against FMD has been prohibited in the EU since 1991, accompanied by a severe import policy to protect the fully FMD-susceptible European cattle. Import is banned from FMD-infected, suspected, or vaccinating countries/regions. Libya was also suspected, in early 2020, of Rift Valley fever infections in small ruminants (by serology).\n\nFor the track of the Karim Allah livestock carrier since 17 Dec 2020, as published by Reuters on 25 Feb 2021, please see\nhttps://fingfx.thomsonreuters.com/gfx/ce/xegpbwewqvq/KarimAllahCarrier.png.\n\nAccording to other reports (The Guardian, Reuters), a 2nd vessel with a consignment of cattle from Spain is returning to Spain; this refers to the Elbeik, which set sail a day after Karim Allah from Tarragona with a cargo of nearly 1800 cattle similarly destined to Turkey. Both vessels were refused unloading in Turkey. On Sat 27 Feb 2021, tracking the website Marine Traffic showed the Elbeik on its way back to Spain, destined for Cartagena. The vessel's return to Spain was confirmed in an email from the Cypriot government's chief veterinary officer, Christodoulos Charalambous Pipis, who has been monitoring the Elbeik. It spent several days anchored off the coast of northern Cyprus, outside the port of Famagusta.\n\nLate last week, a source told the Guardian that of the 1770 or so animals loaded on the Albeik, about 35 might have died, and the rest were in good condition. \"They are limousin and charolais cross [bulls], between 6 and 12 months old,\" the source said.\n\nRepresentatives from the Karim Allah and Elbeik argued that they were \"100% sure\" the cattle on the ship were bluetongue-free and that \"there was a mistake on the Spanish animal health paperwork. That is how this all started. They wrote Aragon [as the cattle's origin]. Aragon is not free of bluetongue the last 24 months.\" According to them, the animals were not from Aragon, but from Zaragoza and Teruel, which are \"150 km away from the focus [of the bluetongue areas],\" and met the requirement of having come from a bluetongue-free area.\n\nThe Spanish agriculture ministry previously told the Guardian that the ships' situation had \"nothing to do with the actions of the Spanish administration\" and that the cattle had come from areas free of bluetongue.\n\nOn 24 Nov 2020, Spain reported to the OIE 4 outbreaks of BTV-8 affecting cattle, located in Pais Vasco/Basque Country (2), Aragon (1) and Navarra (1).\n\nThe whole event may be reminiscent of the 2012 Ocean Drover event, when a sheep consignment from Australia to the Gulf states was rejected due to animal health reservations, eventually ending up in Pakistan after being anchored off a Bahrain port for at least a fortnight. Return to Australia was rejected by the Australian authorities. Testing on arrival in Pakistan cleared the sheep of ill-health concerns (see 20121004.1325036, 20120917.1297467). - Mod.AS\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nSpain: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/43]\nSee Also\n2020\n----\nBluetongue - Europe (13): Spain (NA) cattle, BTV-8, OIE 20201127.7976507\nFoot & mouth disease - Libya: (TR) sheep, st A, OIE 20200401.7168461\nRift Valley fever - Libya (03): (WS, WH) spread, small ruminants, OIE, RFI 20200229.7035852\nRift Valley fever - Libya (02): (KU) spread, small ruminants, OIE, RFI 20200213.6986855\nRift Valley fever - Libya: (KU) 1st report, serology, small ruminants, OIE 20200115.6891516\n2018\n----\nBluetongue - Turkey: (AA) ovine, st 8 & 4, OIE 20181121.6157808\n2017\n----\nBluetongue - Europe (11): Turkey, ovine, caprine, serotypes 4, 16, OIE, RFI 20171212.5496944\n2012\n----\nImported sheep - Pakistan ex Australia (03): multiple problems 20121004.1325036\nContagious ecthyma, sheep - ex Australia: Bahrain, Pakistan 20120917.1297467\n.................................................sb/arn/msp/lxl", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8221269", "headline": "Koala retrovirus - Australia: update", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8221269", "date": "2021-03-01 16:03:39", "main_text": "KOALA RETROVIRUS - AUSTRALIA: UPDATE\n************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Fri 26 Feb 2021\nSource: Daily Mail [edited]\nhttps://www.dailymail.co.uk/sciencetech/article-9304047/Koala-bears-infected-virus-causes-cancer.html\n\n\nKoala bears are infected with a virus which is inserting itself into their DNA and causing cancer, a study has found.\n\nThe marsupials are native to Australasia [and South America], only eat eucalyptus and have a range of health issues, including chlamydia and cancers such as leukaemia and lymphoma. They are also being dramatically impacted by wildfires and habitat loss.\n\nWhile it is known that chlamydia is widespread among koalas, the cause of their cancers has long been a mystery. Researchers from Leibniz Institute for Zoo and Wildlife Research in Berlin studied the DNA of 10 koalas and found a retrovirus embedded in their genome. HIV, which causes AIDS, is the most commonly known human retrovirus.\n\nThe genome-altering virus has infected the cells of koalas which create eggs and sperm, allowing the virus to be passed down the generations.\n\nKoala retrovirus (KoRV) often inserts itself at 'hot spots' which are near genes linked with cancer, and the researchers think the mutations brought about by the virus increases the prevalence of certain cancers.\n\nRemains of ancient retrovirus infections are commonly seen in the genomes of many vertebrates. These retrovirus relics indicate the infection occurred millions of years ago and has since been neutralised.\n\nBut analysis of 10 cancer-riddled koalas from the wild reveals the marsupial population only 1st became infected with KoRV around 50 000 years ago. Since then it has spread and it is now found in every koala in Queensland and New South Wales.\n\nThe DNA samples revealed each koala has around 80 - 100 inherited copies of KoRV in its genome. 'The genomic locations of most of these are not shared between koalas, indicating a rapid expansion and accumulation of KoRV copies in the population,' says Professor Alex Greenwood, head of wildlife diseases at the Leibniz-IZW.\n\n'Each time a retrovirus copies and re-inserts itself into the genome, it causes a mutation, potentially disrupting gene expression, which could be detrimental to the host.'\n\nAs the virus spreads throughout a koala it slowly rewrites more of the koala's genome and replaces its original DNA. The German team found a copy of KoRV had incorporated an entire cancer-related gene into one koala's DNA sequence.\n\nThe analysis also suggests KoRV predisposes koalas to particular tumours and these genes can then also be inherited by their offspring.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Before the discovery of the koala endogenous retrovirus (KoRV), mammalian endogenous retrovirus were thought not to produce infectious particles. KoRV retains its ability to form virus particles capable of 'de novo' horizontal infection transmission. Due to this, it is thought to be undergoing a process of 'endogenization'.\n\nRecent investigations in koalas kept in zoos revealed the existence of 4 subtypes of KoRV, KoRV-A, KoRV-B, and KoRV-J. Different subtypes have different traits in their transmission and pathogenicity.\n\nA recent study (https://www.pnas.org/content/117/17/9529) described the 1st exogenous retrovirus in bats, the Hervey pteropid gammaretrovirus (HPG) in northeast Australia. Koala populations are currently in severe decline and at risk from KoRV, which is closely related to HPG. HPG is also related to the gibbon ape leukemia virus (GALV), which suggests that the origins of KoRV and GALV are spill-over from bats.\n\nKoalas are at an early state of the endogenization process of KoRV, and so the extinction of the exogenous retroviral counterpart and genomic fixation may not be reached for hundreds of years. Until that happens, koalas must endure and overcome the impact on their health, including increased cancer rates.\n\nResearch article referenced:\nMcEwen GK, Alquezar-Planas DE, Dayaram A, et al. Retroviral integrations contribute to elevated host cancer rates during germline invasion. Nature Communications Feb 2021, 12: 1316 DOI: https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-021-21612-7. - Mod.PMB\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nAustralia: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/186]\nSee Also\n2020\n----\nKoala retrovirus - Australia: bat origin 20200415.7227708\n2013\n----\nKoala retrovirus - Japan: novel serogroup 20130708.1811946\nKoala retrovirus - USA: (CA) lymphoma, leukemia 20130627.1795093\n2004\n----\nRetrovirus, koalas - Australia (QLD) 20040719.1954\n1995\n----\nKoala retroviruses 19950407.0187\n.................................................sb/pmb/ao/lxl", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8219679", "headline": "COVID-19 update (83): summary tidbits, intellectual property, holistic model, WHO", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8219679", "date": "2021-03-01 09:26:51", "main_text": "CORONAVIRUS DISEASE 2019 UPDATE (83): SUMMARY TIDBITS, INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY, HOLISTIC MODEL, WHO, GLOBAL\n*********************************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nIn this update:\n[1] Global summary tidbits\n[2] WHO: intellectual property rules\n[3] Research: holistic model of SARS-CoV-2; spike proteins move in tandem\n[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 28 Feb 2021)\n[5] Global update: Worldometer accessed 28 Feb 2021 23:29 EST (GMT-5)\n\n******\n[1] Global summary tidbits\nDate: Sun 28 Feb 2021\nSource: Deutsche Welle (DW) [abridged, edited]\nhttps://www.dw.com/en/coronavirus-digest-germany-to-tighten-controls-at-french-border/a-56727786\n\n\nEurope\n------\n- Germany has added France's eastern Moselle region to its list of \"variant of concern\" areas, triggering tougher entry requirements at the border between the 2 neighbors. Under the new restrictions, almost all travel will be banned. There are only a few exemptions, including lorry drivers and certain key workers. Anyone crossing the border will have to provide a valid negative COVID-19 test. Earlier this month [February 2021], Germany added the Czech Republic and Tyrol in Austria to its list of hotspots where the UK and South African variants -- thought to be more contagious -- are spreading. Entry bans targeting those areas caused long tailbacks on motorways leading to the German border. The travel restrictions for Moselle are due to take effect from Tuesday [2 Mar 2021].\n\n- The majority of people in Germany are still in support of the current lockdown measures, but the share has been slowly dropping, a poll published on Sunday [28 Feb 2021] by the Welt am Sonntag. The share of the population which considered the coronavirus measures appropriate was at 63% in February [2021], down from 69% in November [2020] and 73% in September [2020]. Germany's Robert Koch Institute reported 7890 new cases in the past 24 hours on Sunday [28 Feb 2021]. There were also 157 coronavirus deaths reported -- this brought the total number of deaths in the country since the beginning of the pandemic to over 70 000.\n\n- Britain's government says families with children in school will be provided with free twice-weekly coronavirus home test kits, regardless of whether anyone has symptoms. The tests will be offered as part of plans for schools to reopen, beginning on [Mon 8 Mar 2021].\n\n- Hungarian Prime Minister Viktor Orban has been vaccinated against coronavirus, he announced on his official Facebook page on Sunday [28 Feb 2021]. He received the shot developed by China's Sinopharm pharmaceutical company.\n\n- Danish police have arrested 8 people at an anti-lockdown demonstration in Copenhagen. The largely peaceful rally late Saturday [27 Feb 2021] was attended by around 1200 people. It was the 1st such protest since the government announced last week that it was extending many anti-coronavirus restrictions. The police said they arrested people for allegedly using fireworks and for rowdy behavior.\n\nAmericas\n--------\n- The US Food and Drug Administration approved the Johnson & Johnson vaccine for emergency use on Saturday evening [27 Feb 2021], making it the 3rd vaccine to be given the green light in the country.\n\n- Thousands of Argentinians gathered in front of government buildings in Buenos Aires on Saturday [27 Feb 2021] evening to protest \"vaccine privileges.\" The revelation that people close to the minister of health had been able to jump the queue sparked outrage and ended with the minister losing his position.\n\nAfrica\n------\n- Nigeria expects to become the 3rd West African country to receive vaccines from the COVAX program. It is expecting 3.92 million doses in the shipment. The country is expecting 16 million overall doses in the next few months from COVAX. The country plans to vaccinate 40% of its some 200 million people by the end of the year [2021], and 30% more in 2022.\n\n- South African president Cyril Ramaphosa said there is an agreement to secure 11 million Johnson & Johnson vaccines through the end of the year. About 1/4 of those vaccines would come in the 2nd quarter of 2021. Ramaphosa added that the cabinet decided to ease restrictions on movement due to a drop in cases, downgrading the national alert level from 3 to 1.\n\nAsia and Oceania\n----------------\n- Iran's coronavirus fatalities broke the 60 000 mark on Sunday [28 Feb 2021] after a further 93 people died in 24 hours, according to the Health Ministry. The Islamic Republic is battling the Middle East's worst outbreak of the illness.\n\n- Residents in New Zealand's biggest city Auckland woke up on Sunday [28 Feb 2021] to a 2nd lockdown this month [February 2021]. The 7-day lockdown was announced by Prime Minister Jacinda Ardern after a community coronavirus case was found with no links to a previous cluster. The person had also been infectious for a week but was not in isolation, fueling concerns that there could be additional cases [apparently the case was connected to the case earlier in February 2021, according to the other cases' family https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/124390078/covid19-case-n-went-for-a-walk-with-mother-in-cluster-household-during-alert-level-3.]\n\n- Thailand launched its vaccination program on Sunday [28 Feb 2021], administering doses of the Chinese SinoVac vaccine to frontline health and medical workers as well as cabinet ministers. Prime Minister Prayuth Chan-ocha, 66, fell outside of the age range of the SinoVac vaccine -- 18-59 -- and so did not receive a dose.\n\n- The Philippines has received its 1st batch of COVID-19 vaccines. The 600 000 doses were donated by China. The country is among the last in Southeast Asia to secure the critical doses despite having the 2nd-highest number of coronavirus infections and deaths in the hard-hit region.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Rapporteur Kunihiko Iizuka\n\n[Other developments in Africa: Ghana became the \"1st country to receive COVID-19 vaccines through the World Health Organization's COVAX program on Wednesday [24 Feb 2021], a joint statement issued by UNICEF Ghana and WHO Ghana said.\n\nThe vaccines were produced by the Serum Institute of India, in the Indian city of Pune, and are part of the 1st wave of COVID-19 vaccines headed to low and middle-income countries, the joint statement added. \"Today marks the historic moment for which we have been planning and working so hard,\" said UNICEF Executive Director Henrietta Fore. \"With the 1st shipment of doses, we can make good on the promise of the COVAX facility to ensure people from less wealthy countries are not left behind in the race for life-saving vaccines.\"\n(Excerpted from https://www.cnn.com/2021/02/24/africa/ghana-covax-vaccine-intl/index.html)]\n\n\"Ivory Coast received a shipment of COVID-19 doses from the COVAX vaccine-sharing facility on Friday [26 Feb 2021], becoming the 2nd country to benefit from a programme meant to ensure fairer distribution amid a global scramble. A plane carrying 504 000 doses touched down in the commercial capital Abidjan, paving the way for the West African nation to launch a vaccination campaign next week.\n\n\"By the end of this year [2021], COVAX plans to deliver nearly 2 billion doses to over 90 low- and middle-income countries, hoping to level a playing field that has seen wealthier nations vaccinate millions while comparatively few have received shots in poorer parts of the world.\"\n(Excerpted from https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-ivorycoast-vaccine-idUSKBN2AQ1CZ)]. - Mod.LK]\n\n******\n[2] WHO: intellectual property rules\nDate: Fri 26 Feb 2021\nSource: Al Jazeera, Reuters report [edited]\nhttps://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/2/26/vaccine-hoarding-threatens-global-supply-via-covax-who\n\n\nCOVAX: WHO\n----------\nWHO chief urges countries to waive intellectual property rules, to allow others to make vaccines more quickly. WHO Director-General Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus says 'we can't beat COVID without vaccine equity'26 Feb 2021 Countries seeking their own COVID-19 vaccine doses are making deals with drug companies that threaten the supply for the global COVAX programme for poor and middle-income countries, the World Health Organization (WHO) said on Fri [26 Feb 2021].\n\n\"Now, some countries are still pursuing deals that will compromise the COVAX supply. Without a doubt,\" WHO senior adviser Bruce Aylward told a briefing.\n\nThe WHO has long called upon rich countries to ensure that vaccines are shared equitably. The global organisation is one of the leaders of COVAX, a programme that aims to supply 1.3 billion vaccine doses to poor and middle-income countries this year. But so far, COVAX has had a slow roll-out. \"We can't beat COVID without vaccine equity. Our world will not recover fast enough without vaccine equity, this is clear,\" WHO Director-General Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus said.\n\n\"We have made great progress. But that progress is fragile. We need to accelerate the supply and distribution of COVID-19 vaccines, and we cannot do that if some countries continue to approach manufacturers who are producing vaccines that COVAX is counting on.\"\n\n\"These actions undermine COVAX and deprive health workers and vulnerable people around the world of life-saving vaccines.\"\n\nThe Ivory Coast received its 1st batch of coronavirus vaccines under the COVAX scheme on Friday [26 Feb 2021]\n\nIntellectual property plea Tedros also called for countries to waive intellectual property rules, to allow other countries to make vaccines more quickly. \"If not now, when?\" he asked.\n\nThe idea of temporarily waiving intellectual property rights for tools to fight COVID-19 is set to come up again next week at a meeting of World Trade Organization (WTO) member states. In the past, it has run into opposition from rich countries with big pharmaceutical industries.\n\nIncoming WTO head Ngozi Okonjo-Iweala of Nigeria has said her top priority would be to ensure the trade body does more to address the COVID-19 pandemic, calling disparities in vaccine rates between rich and poor \"unconscionable\".\n\nThe 164-member WTO body usually has to agree by consensus unless members agree to proceed to a rare vote.\n\nSeparately, the WHO said Nigeria is expecting its 1st 4 million doses of coronavirus vaccines next week via COVAX. Walter Kazadi Mulombo, head of WHO's mission in Nigeria, told a briefing by video link that Nigeria was expecting 14 million doses in total.\n\nChikwe Ihekweazu, Director General of the Nigeria Centre for Disease Control (NCDC), said the situation in Nigeria was so far much better than had been widely predicted early in the pandemic.\n\nNigeria, Africa's most populous country with some 200 million people, has reported fewer than 1900 COVID-19 deaths so far.\n\n\"The whole world expected the continent of Africa, and Nigeria with our social and economic realities, to basically fall apart,\" Ihekweazu told the briefing.\n\nHe also referred to the findings of seroprevalence studies, published on Monday [22 Feb 2021], which suggested that 23 percent of Lagos state inhabitants -- around 4 million people -- may have had COVID-19 in October [2020].\n\nHe said studies in 4 Nigerian states had shown that serious illness appeared to be rarer than feared, possibly in part because of the young average age of the population.\n\n\"Getting the vaccine into Nigeria will serve the continent well, will serve the world well,\" he said.\n\nNigeria plans to inoculate 40 percent of the population this year [2021] and 30 percent more in 2022.\n\nIhekweazu said authorities recognised the need for equity in access to vaccines and was committed to pursuing multilateral deals.\n\n\"We will not look for bilateral deals,\" Ihekweazu said.\n\n\"We will work in a multilateral way with WHO, with COVAX with the African Union (AU) to make sure that as we get vaccines into Nigeria, the same happens ... across the continent,\" he said.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[It is important to control COVID-19 and fair to the people that low- and middle-income countries have equal access to the vaccine. The COVAX programme aims to supply 1.3 billion vaccine doses to poor and middle-income countries this year. (2021). Because of competition for vaccines, this program presents a challenge. It is up to the wealthier countries to ensure this takes place, but it is unlikely countries will agree to waive intellectual property rules, to allow others to make vaccines more quickly.\n\nAccording to the WHO, COVAX offers:\n- \"Doses for at least 20% of countries' populations\n- Diverse and actively managed portfolio of vaccines\n- Vaccines delivered as soon as they are available\n- End the acute phase of the pandemic\n- Rebuild economies\"\n- Mod LK]\n\n******\n[3] Research: holistic model of SARS-CoV-2; spike proteins move in tandem\nDate: Sun 28 Feb 2021\nSource: HPC Wire [abridged, edited]\nhttps://www.hpcwire.com/2021/02/28/supercomputers-enable-first-holistic-model-of-sars-cov-2-showing-spike-proteins-move-in-tandem/\n\n\nMost models of SARS-CoV-2, the coronavirus that causes COVID-19, hone in on key features of the virus: for instance, the spike protein. Some of this is attributable to the relative importance of those features, but most is attributable to computational necessity -- simulating even a single protein in such excruciating resolution is extraordinarily computation-intensive. Now, researchers from the University of Chicago and the University of California, San Diego have developed the 1st complete model of the coronavirus, finding, among other things, that its spike proteins move cooperatively.\n\n\"We wanted to understand how SARS-CoV-2 works holistically as a whole particle,\" said Gregory Voth, a professor of chemistry at the University of Chicago and corresponding author of the study, in an interview with Jorge Salazar of the Texas Advanced Computing Center (TACC). \"We developed a bottom-up coarse-grained model where we took information from atomistic-level molecular dynamics simulations and from experiments.\"\n\nVoth and his colleagues have been using the coarse-grained modeling method, which resolves groups of atoms rather than each individual atom, to study viruses like HIV and the flu for decades. \"The benefit of the coarse-grained model is that it can be hundreds to thousands of times more computationally efficient than the all-atom model,\" he said. \"What you're left with are the much slower, collective motions. The effects of the higher frequency, all-atom motions are folded into those interactions if you do it well. That's the idea of systematic coarse-graining.\"\n\nUsing the coarse-graining method, the team simplified and combined atomistic models of SARS-CoV-2's spike, membrane, nucleocapsid, and envelope proteins. Some of these all-atom models were generated by the Amaro Lab (led by Gordon Bell Special Prize winner Rommie Amaro) using the 23.5 Linpack petaflops Frontera supercomputer at TACC, and the remaining models were generated on the Anton 2 system at the Pittsburgh Supercomputing Center (PSC).\n\n\"Frontera and Anton 2 provided the key molecular level input data into this model,\" Voth said. \"Frontera has been especially useful in providing the molecular dynamics data at the atomistic level for feeding into this model. It's very valuable.\"\n\nThe supercomputer-powered coarse-grained model showed some interesting behavior: the virus' spike proteins, which litter its surface and allow it to infect human cells, move cooperatively.\n\n\"They don't move independently like a bunch of random, uncorrelated motions. They work together,\" Voth said. \"The paper we published shows the beginnings of how the modes of motion in the spike proteins are correlated.\n\nThe ultimate goal of the model would be, as a 1st step, to study the initial virion attractions and interactions with ACE2 receptors on cells and to understand the origins of that attraction and how those proteins work together to go on to the virus fusion process.\"\n\n[Byline: Oliver Peckham]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Reference\n----------\nYu A, Pak AJ, He P, et al. A multiscale coarse-grained model of the SARS-CoV-2 virion. Biophys J. 2020 Nov 28:S0006-3495(20)33168-4. doi: 10.1016/j.bpj.2020.10.048. Epub ahead of print. PMID: 33253634; PMCID: PMC7695975.\nhttps://www.cell.com/biophysj/fulltext/S0006-3495(20)33168-4 (abridged)\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\"Abstract\n---------\n\"The severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2 (SARS-CoV-2) is the causative agent of the COVID-19 pandemic. Computer simulations of complete viral particles can provide theoretical insights into large-scale viral processes including assembly, budding, egress, entry, and fusion. Detailed atomistic simulations are constrained to shorter timescales and require billion-atom simulations for these processes. Here, we report the current status and ongoing development of a largely \"bottom-up\" coarse-grained (CG) model of the SARS-CoV-2 virion. Data from a combination of cryo-electron microscopy (cryo-EM), x-ray crystallography, and computational predictions were used to build molecular models of structural SARS-CoV-2 proteins, which were then assembled into a complete virion model. We describe how CG molecular interactions can be derived from all-atom simulations, how viral behavior difficult to capture in atomistic simulations can be incorporated into the CG models, and how the CG models can be iteratively improved as new data become publicly available. Our initial CG model and the detailed methods presented are intended to serve as a resource for researchers working on COVID-19 who are interested in performing multiscale simulations of the SARS-CoV-2 virion.\n\n\"Significance\n-------------\n\"This study reports the construction of a molecular model for the SARS-CoV-2 virion and details our multiscale approach toward model refinement. The resulting model and methods can be applied to and enable the simulation of SARS-CoV-2 virions.\n\n\"A holistic model of the SARS-CoV-2 virion can provide insight into the mechanisms of large-scale viral processes and the collective behavior of macromolecules involved in viral replication and infectivity.\"\n- Mod.LK]\n\n******\n[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 28 Feb 2021)\nDate: Sun 28 Feb 2021\nSource: WHO [abridged, edited]\nhttps://covid19.who.int/table\n\n\n*Daily case reports as of 28 Feb 2021 18:31 CET\n\nSurveillance\n------------\nWHO region (no. countries/territories):\nTotal confirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\n---------------------------------------\nWestern Pacific Region (19): 1 620 580 (6983) / 29 006 (114)\nEuropean Region (61): 38 674 452 (139 264) / 861 803 (2296)\nSouth East Asia Region (10): 13 517 009 (24 114) / 208 013 (317)\nEastern Mediterranean Region (22): 6 388 249 (27 904) / 144 479 (339)\nRegion of the Americas (54): 50 426 060 (179 480) / 1 205 245 (4920)\nAfrican Region (49): 2 840 208 (7211) / 71 991 (244)\nCases on an international conveyance (Diamond Princess): 745 (0) / 13 (0)\n\nConfirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\nGrand total: 113 467 303 (384 956) / 2 520 550 (8230)\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Data by country, area, or territory for 28 Feb 2021 can be accessed at https://promedmail.org/wp-content/uploads/world-pdf/WHO%20COVID%20update%2028%20Feb%202021_1614557361.pdf.\n\n- The Americas region reported 46.6% of daily case numbers and 59.8% of the daily deaths reported in the past 24 hours and maintained its position as the most severely affected region, having reported more than 50.42 million cases. AFRICA\n************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nIn this update:\n[1] USA\n[2] Guinea: caregivers\n[3] Sub-Saharan Africa: Spillover events\n\n******\n[1] USA\n- Fri 26 Feb 2021. Monitoring travelers\nCBS News (abridged, edited)\nhttps://www.cbsnews.com/news/ebola-monitoring-program-u-s-considering-as-new-cases-reported-in-africa/\n\n\nThe U.S. will soon be monitoring travelers coming into the country from 2 nations impacted by the Ebola virus, the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention announced Fri 26 Feb 2021. The CDC confirmed these plans after CBS News 1st reported the details on Friday [26 Feb 2021] night.\n\nStarting next week, the \"very small number\" of travelers arriving from Guinea and the Democratic Republic of the Congo will be funneled to 6 U.S. airports where their information will be collected and shared with local health officials, the CDC said.\n\nAs of 25 Feb 2021, 9 Ebola cases have been reported in Guinea, resulting in 5 deaths, and 8 cases have been reported in the Democratic Republic of the Congo, resulting in 4 deaths, according to the World Health Organization. The CDC stressed in its statement that \"the outbreaks are centered in remote areas of these countries,\" and said \"the risk of Ebola to the United States is extremely low.\"\n\nThe CDC said airlines \"will collect and transmit passenger information to CDC for public health follow-up and intervention for all passengers boarding a flight to the U.S. who were in DRC or Guinea within the previous 21 days. This information will be shared with U.S. state and local health departments to appropriately monitor arrivals in their jurisdiction.\"\n\nA source familiar with the decision said John F. Kennedy in New York, Dulles outside Washington, D.C., O'Hare in Chicago, Hartsfield-Jackson in Atlanta, Los Angeles International Airport and Newark Liberty outside New York were all being considered as monitoring points. The CDC did not specify which airports it plans to use.\n\nThis funneling approach is similar to steps taken in 2014 when travelers from Liberia, Sierra Leone and Guinea were directed to 5 of those airports, where they had their temperature taken upon arrival.\n\nBetween March 2014 and April 2016, there were more than 28 000 cases of Ebola in West Africa, and 11 310 people died, according to the CDC.\n\nWith the ongoing COVID-19 pandemic, there is recognition within the CDC that resources for additional monitoring are stretched thin, according to one of the people familiar with the discussions. Almost 30 000 people were monitored by the CDC for Ebola beginning in 2014, an effort that required hundreds of CDC staff, the CDC said.\n\n\"This is a great example of how we have to be prepared for anything in the public health arena,\" another source familiar with the discussions said about the monitoring before the news was announced.\n\nIn 2014, the Obama administration appointed Ron Klain to lead the U.S. Ebola strategy. Klain is now President Biden's chief of staff.\n\n[Byline: Bo Erickson, Corey Rangel and Ed O'Keefe]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n[Diverting and monitoring for Ebola in US travelers from the DRC and Guinea when there are only a handful of cases seems overly cautious and an added burden on public health personnel at a time when there is tremendous pressure from COVID. Resources are already stretched thin. The situation is very different from that occurring during the 2014 outbreak in West Africa. Certainly, medical personnel should be alerted to the ongoing outbreak in the DRC and Guinea so they can be certain their hospitals and staff are prepared to respond immediately should a potential patient be identified. - Mod.LK]\n\n----\n- Fri 26 Feb 2021. US: risk low\nReuters (edited)\nhttps://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-usa-cdc/u-s-cdc-says-risk-of-ebola-to-the-united-states-is-extremely-low-idUSKBN2AR032?rpc=401&\n\n\nThe U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention said it was closely following outbreaks of Ebola in Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC) and Guinea and said the risk of Ebola to the United States was extremely low.\n\n\"Out of an abundance of caution, the U.S. government will institute public health measures for the very small number of travelers arriving from the DRC and Guinea,\" the CDC said in a statement late on Fri 26 Feb 2021.\n\n\"The Biden Administration is committed to working closely with the affected countries to end these outbreaks before they grow into epidemics,\" the CDC said.\n\nGuinea started an Ebola vaccination campaign on Tue [23 Feb 2021], the World Health Organization said earlier in the week, as authorities race to contain the 1st resurgence of the virus there since the world's worst outbreak in 2013-2016.\n\nThe resurgence of the virus, which causes severe bleeding and organ failure and is spread through contact with body fluids, has alarmed governments in the region and international health organizations, concerned that a major outbreak could overwhelm health infrastructures already battling a pandemic.\n\nThe CDC said on Fri 26 Feb 2021 that beginning next week, travelers from DRC and Guinea will be funneled to 6 U.S. airports. Airlines will collect passenger information for public health follow-up and intervention for all passengers boarding a flight to the U.S. who were in DRC or Guinea within the previous 21 days.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n******\n[2] Guinea: Caregivers\n- 26 Feb 2021\nDaily Mail (abridged, edited)\nhttps://www.dailymail.co.uk/wires/afp/article-9305209/In-Ebola-stricken-Guinea-caregivers-no-risks.html\n\n\nEbola causes severe fever and, in the worst cases, unstoppable bleeding. It is transmitted through close contact with bodily fluids, and people who live with or care for patients are most at risk.\n\nHigh mortality rates, and harrowing memories of the previous outbreak, has made some in Nzerekore reticent about seeking treatment. However the prognosis appears better this time around.\n\nAt least 5 people have died in the latest outbreak, according to the country's health agency, although there is some confusion over the exact death toll.\n\nGuinean health authorities have also reported 10 confirmed or probable Ebola cases and are tracking 400 more contact cases.\n\nThe country also launched a vaccination campaign against Ebola this week, a treatment which was unavailable during the last epidemic.\n\nGuinea's government, medical NGOs, and the World Health Organization mobilised quickly after news of the outbreak. Vaccinations began only a week after the outbreak was confirmed, and medical teams were rapidly deployed to Nzerekore. The treatment centre there consists of a small compound of several buildings painted yellow and red, surrounded by a metal grating.\n\n\"People need to understand that an Ebola treatment centre is not a hospice,\" said Dally Muamba, a doctor employed at the centre by the Alliance for International Medical Action.\n\nHe added that the centre is using a treatment developed in the Democratic Republic of Congo -- where Ebola is endemic -- which involves injecting patients with antibodies extracted from survivors of the disease.\n\n\"Chances of survival are much higher today,\" Muamba says.\n\nAlseny-Modet Camara, the head of the treatment centre, agrees. \"The mortality rate was up to 70 percent before we were able to reduce that mortality to less than 10 percent,\" he said.\n\nA middle-aged man emerges from one of the small buildings with his eyes downcast, drips in both arms, and sits on a plastic chair. The man has just learned he has Ebola. An Ebola survivor from the 1st epidemic, nicknamed \"Dr Papus,\" broke the news to him, and tried to reassure him. \"I tell them that I have faced this disease, that we must not give up,\" says Papus, whose father and uncle both died of Ebola in 2014.\n\nHe says he did not believe in the epidemic until he fell ill, and subsequently recovered. \"Since I am already immune, I have to help others, I have to go back and face this demon again,\" he says.\n\nBut not everyone survives. On Thu 25 Feb 2021 evening, a Red Cross pick-up truck arrived at the centre, its paintwork faded from repeat disinfections. It had come to remove the body of a patient who had succumbed to Ebola and whose burial will also be subject to strict medical precautions.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n[See map: https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2021/02/26/19/wire-39813532-1614367679-314_634x599.jpg, where Guinea's latest Ebola outbreak occurred.\n\nThe response this time was very fast. But the problem now seems to fall on diagnosis: early and rapid diagnosis is needed to prevent a patient from going to multiple healthcare centers for medical help. If rapid tests were in stock in clinics in countries where Ebola is enzootic/endemic and doctors were trained to use them if Ebola is even remotely suspected when the patient presents with fever and bleeding, that would be a good practice. It could prevent spread beyond the initial site. - Mod LK]\n\n******\n[3] Sub-Saharan Africa: Spillover events\n- 24 Feb 2021\nForbes (abridged, edited)\nhttps://apple.news/AqaOTkhBpSdyxuM1VZS_OqA\n\n\nI reported recently on the 2 new outbreaks of Ebola in Sub-Saharan Africa. At the time, there were 4 cases in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) and 8 cases in Guinea. Since then, another 2 or 3 cases have been found in the DRC.\n\nThis is the 12th Ebola epidemic in the DRC, and the 2nd in Guinea.\n\nEbola is a zoonotic pathogen, meaning that the virus is maintained in a wild animal species, or reservoir. Under conditions that aren't particularly well understood, it periodically spills over from animal populations into people. Ebola 1st came to global attention in 2015 during the West Africa epidemic that spread widely throughout Guinea, Liberia, and Sierra Leone, and less extensively in Italy, Mali, Nigeria, Senegal, Spain, the UK, and the USA.\n\nA map published in the scientific journal PLoS Neglected Tropical Diseases in 2015 [see comment below] shows where Ebola virus outbreaks have historically occurred along with the animal species implicated in the spillover process. The timeline on the right shows when these outbreaks occurred, including an outbreak of an unidentified pathogen in DRC in 1972 that is now suspected to have been Ebola.\n\nIt has been 5 years since that map was published. Since then, there have been 5 more outbreaks, bringing the total to 27, including (1) a 2018 outbreak in Equateur province (DRC); (2) an epidemic that lasted from August 2018 to June 2020 in the Eastern region of Kivu (DRC), which also spread to Uganda; (3) an outbreak last year [2020], again in Equateur province (DRC); and (4) and (5) the new outbreaks in the DRC and Guinea.\n\nThis invites us to ask the question: is the spillover of Ebola increasing in frequency?\n\nIf we look back at just the last 10 years, there have been 9 outbreaks of Ebola since 2010 -- almost one per year -- compared with just 18 in the preceding 38 years, or roughly one every other year.\n\nFrom this point of view, it certainly looks like Ebola outbreaks have been increasing in frequency. But another look at the timeline shows a curiosity. Ebola seems to have been in a lull with no reported human cases between 1980 and 1993. (There were, however, a few outbreaks in non-human primates in the early 1990s). Viewed this way, one might think of Ebola as having 3 epochs:\n\n1972-1979: 5 outbreaks in 8 years\n1980-1993: 0 outbreaks in 14 years\n1994-present: 22 outbreaks in 28 years.\n\nThe average time between outbreaks in each of these epochs is shown in the following figure [see URL].\n\nFrom this perspective, the frequency of outbreaks now is not meaningfully different than it was in the 1970s, when Ebola was described. So, which historical view is correct? Either way, we have a mystery to solve.\n\nIf we take the timeline view, considering each outbreak, it seems that, indeed, Ebola spillover events are increasing in frequency. Why? What is happening to cause the increase in outbreaks? One hypothesis concerns environmental change, as Ebola outbreaks seem to correlate with shifts in vegetation and the transition between dry and wet seasons. Another explanation concerns the frequency of encounters between humans and wild animals, perhaps because of land conversion or increased demand for animal protein from hunting.\n\nHowever, if we take the epochal view, grouping outbreaks into distinct periods, then there would seem to be no evidence for an increase.\n\nHowever, there is the mystery of the lull in the 1980s and early 1990s. Why would there not have been any outbreaks for 14 years when they occurred every one to 2 years on either side of this period? Did we simply miss them for some reason or were there really that many fewer outbreaks?\n\nIn either case, it is reasonable to expect that Ebola will continue to spill over into human populations. Identifying spillover risk factors, developing surveillance systems for early detection, and securing healthcare and public health resources for rapid response are needed to protect against future Ebola epidemics. Fortunately, the benefits of these investments also have a kind of \"spillover,\" providing protection not only from Ebola but other endemic and emerging diseases too.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nMary Marshall\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n[Alexander KA, Sanderson CE, Marathe M, et al. What Factors Might Have Led to the Emergence of Ebola in West Africa? PLoS NTD Published: 4 Jun 2015 https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pntd.0003652.\n\nAbstract:\n\"An Ebola outbreak of unprecedented scope emerged in West Africa in December 2013 and presently continues unabated in the countries of Guinea, Sierra Leone, and Liberia. Ebola is not new to Africa, and outbreaks have been confirmed as far back as 1976. The current West African Ebola outbreak is the largest ever recorded and differs dramatically from prior outbreaks in its duration, number of people affected, and geographic extent. The emergence of this deadly disease in West Africa invites many questions, foremost among these: why now, and why in West Africa? Here, we review the sociological, ecological, and environmental drivers that might have influenced the emergence of Ebola in this region of Africa and its spread throughout the region. Containment of the West African Ebola outbreak is the most pressing, immediate need. A comprehensive assessment of the drivers of Ebola emergence and sustained human-to-human transmission is also needed in order to prepare other countries for importation or emergence of this disease. Such assessment includes identification of country-level protocols and interagency policies for outbreak detection and rapid response, increased understanding of cultural and traditional risk factors within and between nations, delivery of culturally embedded public health education, and regional coordination and collaboration, particularly with governments and health ministries throughout Africa. Public health education is also urgently needed in countries outside of Africa in order to ensure that risk is properly understood and public concerns do not escalate unnecessarily. To prevent future outbreaks, coordinated, multiscale, early warning systems should be developed that make full use of these integrated assessments, partner with local communities in high-risk areas, and provide clearly defined response recommendations specific to the needs of each community.\"\n\nCertainly, lessons have been learned from and since the 2013 West African outbreak. In addition, vaccines are now available as are effective antivirals. Treatment of patients is greatly improved. But equally important are communication and education, which must be maintained as well as public health infrastructure. Resources should be committed to maintaining clinics, which can be used for other endemic diseases once an outbreak ends. Training of staff should continue.\n\nWith these practices, should Ebola re-emerge, the community will be well prepared to respond immediately. - Mod.LK]\nSee Also\nEbola update (19): Guinea (NZ), (23): comment, pregnant women, news, research 20160316.4098040\n.................................................lk/msp/mpp", "reports": []}, {"archive_id": "8217634", "headline": "Avian influenza, human (03): Russia, H5N8, update", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8217634", "date": "2021-02-28 16:38:06", "main_text": "AVIAN INFLUENZA, HUMAN (03): RUSSIA, H5N8, UPDATE\n*************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: 26 Feb 2021\nSource: Disease Outbreak News [edited]\nhttps://www.who.int/csr/don/26-feb-2021-influenza-a-russian-federation/en/\n\n\nOn 18 Feb 2021, the National IHR Focal Point for the Russian Federation notified WHO of detection of avian influenza A(H5N8) in 7 human clinical specimens. These are the 1st reported detections of avian influenza A(H5N8) in humans.\n\nPositive clinical specimens were collected from poultry farm workers who participated in a response operation to contain an avian influenza A(H5N8) outbreak detected in a poultry farm in Astrakhan Oblast in the Russian Federation. The laboratory confirmation of the 7 specimens was performed by the State Research Centre for Virology and Biotechnology VECTOR (WHO H5 Reference Laboratory). The ages of the 7 positive cases ranged between 29 to 60 years, and 5 were female.\n\nBetween 3 and 11 Dec 2020, a total of 101 000 out of 900 000 egg-laying hens on the farm died. This high mortality rate prompted an investigation. Samples were collected from these birds, and an initial detection of avian influenza A(H5N8) was performed by the Russian regional veterinary laboratory. On 11 Dec 2020, the outbreak was confirmed by the World Organisation for Animal Health (OIE) Reference laboratory, and the Federal Centre for Animal Health (FGBI-ARRIAH), in Vladimir, the Russian Federation. Outbreak containment operations started immediately and continued for several days due to the large size of the poultry farm.\n\nThe cases remained asymptomatic for the whole follow up duration (several weeks). Follow up nasopharyngeal swabs were collected during the medical observation period and were tested negative for avian influenza A(H5N8). No obvious clinical manifestations were reported from any farm workers under medical surveillance, their family members, or other close contacts of the 7 cases. Additionally, acute and convalescent sera were collected from the 7 positive human cases for serological testing. The results were suggestive of recent infection.\n\nInfluenza A(H5N8) viruses isolated from this poultry outbreak in Astrakhan belonged to clade 2.3.4.4b of avian influenza A(H5Nx) viruses. In 2020, avian influenza A (H5N8) viruses were also detected in poultry or wild birds in Bulgaria, the Czech Republic, Egypt, Germany, Hungary, Iraq, Japan, Kazakhstan, the Netherlands, Poland, Romania, the United Kingdom, and the Russian Federation.\n\nOn receiving the initial signal of a probable outbreak of highly pathogenic avian influenza (HPAI) at the poultry farm on 3 Dec 2020, the national authorities took immediate measures including cessation of poultry production cycles and product transportation from the affected farm.\n\nBetween 11 and 18 Dec 2020, several measures, including culling and disposing of poultry, eggs, and litter, and disinfection of contaminated premises, were taken as part of outbreak response activities.\n\nDuring and after the culling of all the poultry, nasopharyngeal swabs and serum samples were collected from poultry farm workers and personnel involved in outbreak response at the farm. Surveillance activities, both within and outside of the containment area, were intensified. A total of 24 close contacts of the confirmed cases have been identified and traced. In total, 150 individuals were monitored for clinical indication of respiratory disease, and they received antiviral prophylaxis therapy. No symptoms were reported among these individuals.\n\nWhole Genome Sequencing of avian influenza A (H5N8) viruses isolated from poultry and from one of the 7 human cases was performed and uploaded to the Global Initiative on Sharing All Influenza Data (GISAID) database on 20 Feb 2021. Genetic and phenotypic characterization of the virus is ongoing.\n\nWHO is following up with public health authorities in the Russian Federation, including implementation of public health measures warranted by such events, and with the WHO Global Influenza Surveillance and Response System (GISRS) on further analysis and assessment of the virus materials and serum samples. On 20 Feb 2021, a special briefing by the head of the Federal Service for Surveillance on Consumer Rights Protection and Human Wellbeing was organized for the state Russian media to inform the public about these cases and the implications.\n\nSince 2004, avian influenza A(H5) viruses have spread from Asia to Europe via wild birds. The genetic clade 2.3.4.4 H5 viruses have often reassorted among other avian influenza viruses, resulting in avian influenza A(H5N1), A(H5N2), A(H5N3), A(H5N5), A(H5N6) and A(H5N8) viruses, some of which have been detected in birds in many countries.\n\nIn the Russian Federation, avian influenza A(H5N8) of clade 2.3.4.4 was isolated for the 1st time in 2014 in a wild bird in the northern region of the Russian Far East.\n\nAs mentioned earlier, all the 7 cases with PCR-positive results were clinically asymptomatic. All close contacts of these cases were clinically monitored, and no one showed signs of clinical illness. Infections with avian influenza viruses of the same clade (H5 clade 2.3.4.4) have been reported from China since 2014 in people with exposure to infected birds. The likelihood of human infections with influenza A(H5N8) viruses has been considered to be low.\n\nFurther genetic and antigenic characterization and information on seroconversion among contacts of the positive cases is required to fully assess the risk.\n\nThe development of zoonotic influenza candidate vaccine viruses for potential use in human vaccines, coordinated by WHO, remains an essential component of the overall global strategy for influenza pandemic preparedness.\n\nBased on currently available information, the risk of human-to-human transmission remains low.\n\nThese cases do not change the current WHO recommendations on public health measures and surveillance of animal and seasonal human influenza, which should continue to be implemented. Respiratory transmission occurs mainly by droplets, disseminated by unprotected coughs and sneezes. Short-distance airborne transmission of influenza viruses may occur, particularly in crowded enclosed spaces. Hand contamination, direct inoculation of virus, exposure to infected birds or virus-contaminated materials or environments are potential sources of infection.\n\nWhen avian influenza viruses are circulating in an area, the people involved in specific, high-risk tasks such as sampling sick birds, culling and disposing of infected birds, eggs, and litter, and cleaning of contaminated premises should be trained on how to protect themselves, and on proper use of personal protective equipment (PPE). People involved in these tasks should be registered and monitored closely by local health authorities for 7 days following the last day of contact with poultry or their environments.\n\nDue to the constantly evolving nature of influenza viruses, WHO continues to stress the importance of global surveillance to detect virological, epidemiological and clinical changes associated with circulating influenza viruses that may affect human (or animal) health and timely virus sharing for risk assessment.\n\nThorough investigation of all potential novel influenza human infections is warranted. All human infections caused by a novel influenza subtype are notifiable under the International Health Regulations (IHR), and State Parties to the IHR are required to immediately notify WHO of any laboratory-confirmed case of a recent human infection caused by a new influenza A subtype with the potential to cause a pandemic (please see case definitions for diseases requiring notification under the IHR). Evidence of illness is not required.\n\nIn the case of a confirmed or suspected human infection, a thorough epidemiological investigation of history of exposure to animals, of travel, and contact tracing should be conducted, even while awaiting the confirmatory laboratory results. The epidemiological investigation should include early identification of unusual respiratory events that could signal person-to-person transmission of the novel virus. Clinical samples collected from the time and place that the case occurred should be tested and sent to a WHO Collaboration Center for further characterization.\n\nTravelers to countries with known outbreaks of avian influenza should avoid farms, contact with animals in live animal markets, entering areas where animals may be slaughtered, or contact with any surfaces that appear to be contaminated with animal feces. Travelers should also wash their hands often with soap and water. Travelers should follow good food safety and good food hygiene practices.\n\nBased on the currently available information, WHO advises against any special traveler screening at points of entry or restrictions on travel and/or trade with the Russian Federation.\n\nFor further information and details, please see:\n- Current technical information including monthly risk assessments at the Human-Animal Interface WHO\n- WHO Influenza virus infections in humans October 2018\n- Case definitions for diseases requiring notification under the IHR (2005)\n- International Health Regulations IHR (2005)\n- Manual for the laboratory diagnosis and virological surveillance of influenza (2011)\n- Terms of Reference for National Influenza Centers of the Global Influenza Surveillance and Response System.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED Rapporteur Marianne Hopp\n\n[The above report provides additional details about the 7 human cases of avian influenza A/H5N8 reported almost one week ago. No new cases have been identified since then.\n\nNow that human cases have been reported for this avian influenza subtype, preparedness for future such events requires continued monitoring and surveillance of the circulating viruses in animals and humans. - Mod.UBA]\n\n[According to the Russian report, the 7 individuals found infected by the H5N8 virus strain remained asymptomatic for the whole follow up duration. Checking persons in close contact with HPAI H5N8-affected domestic or wild birds deserves to be undertaken in other affected countries in order to get more information on the zoonotic impact of this widely-spread virus strain. The above report mentions 13 such countries. She said that \"Measles has also been self-isolating\" since the COVID-19 pandemic started.\n\nEven though there has been enhanced surveillance going on regularly in Canada, it has been a full year without any reported cases of the disease. Dr. Tam said that this is \"good news.\"\n\nCanada puts out weekly monitoring reports for measles, and the last reported case was in the week of 2-8 Feb 2020, which was also the only one reported that calendar year.\n\nFlu activity was also down in 2020, with the season ending abruptly in mid-March 2020 because of measures taken to stop COVID-19. Then, in the fall of that year, activity related to the flu was \"exceptionally low.\"\n\n[Byline: Lisa Belmonte]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Social distancing, masks, and school closures have had \"benefits\" not only in preventing spread of SARS-CoV-2, but also other air-borne viruses such as influenza (see next post) and measles. - Mod.LK]\n\n******\n[2] UK: Flu, measles, mumps & rubella infections plummet\nDate: Sat 27 Feb 2021\nSource: CGTN [abridged, edited]\nhttps://newseu.cgtn.com/news/2021-02-27/Flu-measles-mumps-and-rubella-infection-numbers-plummet-in-UK-YcUGRkx6cE/index.html\n\n\nOutbreaks of flu, measles, mumps, and rubella have been almost non-existent in the UK since the outbreak of COVID-19, a batch of scientific data has confirmed.\n\nOut of 685 243 samples tested by Public Health England, not a single case of influenza was detected in the 1st 7 weeks of 2021.\n\nThe imposition of social distancing, combined with the prevalence of face coverings and handwashing, have been credited with blocking the usual routes of transmission for influenza. The reduction in international travel and an increased uptake in the flu vaccine probably also had a major impact.\n\n[Byline: Jim Drury]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n[3] Pakistan: 375 children treated\nDate: Thu 25 Feb 2021\nSource: Relief Web [abridged, edited]\nhttps://reliefweb.int/report/pakistan/375-children-treated-measles-msf-chaman-district-headquarters-hospital\n\n\nSupporting the Department of Health in responding to a measles outbreak, Medecins Sans Frontieres (MSF) is running a 30-bed isolation ward for treatment of measles patients in the District Headquarters (DHQ) Hospital in Chaman, District Qilla Abdullah.\n\nMSF is fully managing the isolation ward through medical staff, medicines, personal protection equipment (PPE), water, power supply, sanitization, and health education.\n\nSince the 1st week of January 2021, when MSF opened the isolation ward, a total of 125 patients have been treated successfully and 250 patients sent home on oral medications. MSF has also vaccinated 756 children for measles since then.\n\nAs there are cases of measles throughout the year in Chaman, MSF already supports the department of health and runs a 5-bed isolation unit inside its pediatric ward in the Qilla Abdullah DHQ hospital.\n\nIts teams started receiving significant numbers of children with measles from the end of December 2020. There were over 1000 cases of measles reported in one month in the district Qilla Abdullah.\n\nMSF medical focal point Dr. Mir Waiz said in a media briefing: \"Our emergency response to the measles outbreak in Chaman is a part of MSF's commitment to supporting the Department of Health in responding to emergencies, including natural disasters and disease outbreaks. We have opened the extended ward for a period of 2 months; however, the treatment of the children with measles will continue in our regular activities. People must take cautionary measures, including isolating patients with measles and getting them treated as soon as possible to stop the outbreak.\"\n\nMost patients recover from measles within 2-3 weeks, but in low-resource settings, up to 15 per cent of patients infected with measles die from one or more complications. Children, especially those under 5 and those who may have other immune-suppressing illnesses, such as severe malnutrition, make up most of those who die from the disease.\n\n\"As vaccination is the best protection against measles, we urge all parents to get their children vaccinated in order to stop the ongoing outbreak of measles and avoid any such emergency situation in the future. We supported the Department of Health's immunization programme to vaccinate 22 830 children for childhood diseases, including 2631 children for measles in 2020,\" added Mir Waiz.\n\nMSF 1st started working in Pakistan in 1986 and now provides urgently needed quality medical care to people in Balochistan, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa, and Sindh provinces. MSF works in collaboration with the health authorities as well as federal, provincial, and local disaster management authorities in the country, and its activities in Pakistan are funded solely by private donations, with no institutional or government contributions.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Qilla Abdullah or Abdullah Qilla is a district in the northwest of Balochistan province of Pakistan.\n\nAlso see:\nMere MO, Goodson JL, Chandio AK, et al. Progress Toward Measles Elimination -- Pakistan, 2000-2018. MMWR Morb Mortal Wkly Rep 2019;68:505-510. DOI: http://dx.doi.org/10.15585/mmwr.mm6822a4external icon:\n\n\"In the 2 decades before 2000, estimated coverage with the 1st measles-containing vaccine dose (MCV1) in Pakistan was 57% or less. The number of reported measles cases per year averaged approximately 29 000 during 1980-1989 and 3900 during 1990-1999.\n\nWhat is added by this report?\nEstimated MCV1 coverage increased from 57% to 76% during 2000-2017, and 2nd-dose coverage increased from 30% to 45% during 2009-2017. Approximately 232.5 million children were vaccinated with MCV during 2005-2018 vaccination campaigns. Despite these efforts, MCV coverage remained well below the recommended level of 95%, and measles incidence increased during 2010-2018.\n\nWhat are the implications for public health practice?\nTo achieve measles elimination, efforts are needed to increase 2-dose vaccine coverage, reach communities not accessing immunization services, and increase measles surveillance sensitivity.\n\nTo advance progress toward measles elimination in Pakistan, there is a need to raise the visibility of measles elimination efforts, including the benefits of achieving measles elimination. Without jeopardizing the focused efforts to interrupt poliovirus transmission, transitioning the substantial polio infrastructure and resources should be carefully managed to support measles elimination and broader EMR vaccination goals.\"\n\nThis report was pre-COVID; consequently, the impact of COVID is not reflected in the numbers. If the measles vaccination campaign could piggyback on the polio immunization program, that would be highly efficient and effective. During COVID, the UAE-Pakistan Assistance Program campaign managed to reach out to some 16 million children and provided over 52 515 000 doses [of polio vaccine] since July 2020 (https://reliefweb.int/report/pakistan/uae-pap-administers-508-mn-doses-polio-vaccine-over-86-mn-children-pakistan-7-years). If measles vaccination could be given at the same time as polio, that would greatly facilitate measles control. - Mod.LK\n\nHealthMap/ProMED maps:\nCanada: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/12\nUnited
